Rulings on Invalid Lease: Wet Nurse and Craftsman's Detention Right
Quduri matn with proofs on wet nurse and craftsman detention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules for a hired wet nurse regarding marital rights and feeding, and explain when a craftsman may detain the object for payment, using Hanafi proofs.

Core Idea
A wet nurse may not be prevented from her husband; a craftsman with trace work may detain the object until paid.

This passage from Quduri's matn on invalid lease (ijarah fasidah) covers two distinct but related topics: the rights and duties of a wet nurse in a fasid hire, and the craftsman's right of retention. Both are supported by proofs from hadith, Quran, and custom. Understanding these distinctions helps ensure contracts are valid and parties are protected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rules for the wet nurse
Extract the three specific rulings: (1) lessee cannot prevent husband's access, (2) she must prepare the child's food, (3) if she uses goat's milk instead of her own, she forfeits wage.
2
Identify the rules for the craftsman
Distinguish between craftsmen whose work leaves a trace (like dyers) and those whose work does not (like porters). The former may detain the object until paid, the latter may not.
3
Locate the proofs for each ruling
For wet nurse: hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij (hiring land), Quran 2:236 (maintenance), and hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions'. For craftsman: statement of al-Sha'bi and the same hadith on conditions.
The hadith on conditions is used for both the nurse and the craftsman.
4
Explain the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
The hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' implies that the terms of the hire contract must be fulfilled. For the craftsman, the condition of payment allows detention as a means to enforce the contract. The Quranic verse on maintenance obligates the nurse to provide food.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute on detention
The Hanafi school restricts detention to trace workers, while the Shafi'i school allows any worker to detain. Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْإِجَارَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ ٢٢ وَلَيْسَ لِلْمُسْتَأْجِرٍ أَنْ يَمَنَعَ زَوْجَهَا مِنْ وَطْئِهَا فَإِنْ حَبِلَتْ كَانَ لَهُمْ أَنْ يَفْسَحُوا الْإِجَارَةَ ٢٣ وَعَلَيْهَا أَنْ تُصْلِحَ طَعَامَ الصَّبِيِّ ٢٤ فَإِنْ أَرْضَعَتْهُ فِي الْمُدَّةِ بِلَبَنِ شَاةٍ فَلَا أَجْرَ لَهَا وَكُلُّ صَانِعِ لِعَمَلِهِ أَثَرٌ فِي الْعَيْنِ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَحْبِسَ الْعَيْنَ بَعْدَ الْفَرَاغِ مِنْ عَمَلِهِ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِي الْأُجْرَةَ كَالصَّبَّاغِ، وَالْقَصَّارِ
٢٥ وَمَنْ لَيْسَ لِعَمَلِهِ أَثَرٌ فِي الْعَيْنِ فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَحْبِسَ الْعَيْنَ كَالْحَمَّالِ، وَالْمَلَاحِ
وجه : (١) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَيْسَ لِلْمُسْتَأْجِرٍ أَنْ يَمَنَعَ زَوْجَهَا مِنْ وَطْبَهَا [؟] سَأَلْتُ رَافِعَ بْنَ خَدِيجٍ عَنْ كِرَاءِ الْأَرْضِ بِالذَّهَبِ وَالْوَرِقِ؟ فَقَالَ: لَا بَأْسَ بِهِ. إِنَّمَا كَانَ النَّاسُ يُؤَاجِرُونَ عَلَى عَهْدِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَى الْمَاذِيَانَاتِ. وَأَقْبَالِ الْجُدَاوِلِ. وَأَشْيَاءَ مِنَ الزَّرْع. فَيَهْلِكُ هَذَا وَيَسْلَمُ هَذَا وَيَسْلَمُ هَذَا وَيَهْلِكُ هذا. فلم يكن الناس كِرَاء إِلَّا هَذَا فَلِذَلِكَ زُجِرَ عَنْهُ فَأَمَّا شيء معلوم مضمون، فلا بأس به، (مسلم شريف: بَاب كِرَاءِ الْأَرْضِ بِالذَّهَبِ وَالْوَرقِ، غمبر 1548)
وجه: (1) الآية الثبوت وَعَلَيْهَا أَنْ تُصْلِحَ طَعَامَ الصَّيّا [؟] ﴿وَمَتِّعُوهُنَّ عَلَى الْمُوسِعِ قَدَرُهُ وَعَلَى الْمُقْتِرِ قَدَرُهُ مَتَاعًا بِالْمَعْرُوفِ حَقًّا عَلَى الْمُحْسِنِينَ ﴾ (سورة البقرة، 2 أيت، نمبر 236)
٢٤ وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ أَرْضَعَتْهُ فِي الْمُدَّةِ بِلَبَنِ شَاةٍ فَلَا أَجْرَ لَنَا [؟] وَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْمُسْلِمُونَ عِنْدَ شُرُوطِهِمْ ، بخاري شريف ، بَابُ أَجْرِ السَّمْسَرَةِ، نمبر 2274)
وجه : (١) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ لَيْسَ لِعَمَلِهِ أَثَرٌ فِي الْعَيْنِ فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَحْبِسَ الْعَيْنَ كَالْحَمَّالِ [؟] ا قَالَ التَّوْرِيُّ: عَنِ الشَّيْبَانِ، عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ قَالَ: «هُوَ ضَامِنٌ فِيمَا خَالَفَ وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ كِرَاءٌ»،((مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ : الْكَرْيُ يَتَعَدَّى بِهِ ، نمبر 14931/بخاري شريف، بَابُ أَجْرِ السمسرة، غير 274636)
وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ لَيْسَ لِعَمَلِهِ أَثَرٌ فِي الْعَيْنِ فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَحْبِسَ الْعَيْنَ كَالْحَمَّالِ وَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْمُسْلِمُونَ عِنْدَ شُرُوطِهِمْ، بخاري شريف بابُ أَجْرِ السَّمْسَرَةِ، غير 2274)
اصول : کام کی تصریح نہ ہوتے وقت عرفِ عام کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔
٢٤ اصول: شرط کی مخالفت کرے تو اجرت نہیں ملے گی۔
Chapter of Invalid Lease. 22. The lessee may not prevent her husband from sexual intercourse with her. If she becomes pregnant, they may cancel the lease. 23. She must prepare the child's food. 24. If she breastfeeds him during the period with goat's milk, she has no wage. And every craftsman whose work leaves a trace on the object has the right to detain the object after finishing his work until he receives the wage, like the dyer and the fuller. 25. And whoever's work does not leave a trace on the object has no right to detain the object, like the porter and the boatman. Proof: (1) Statement of a Companion to establish: The lessee may not prevent her husband... I asked Rafi' ibn Khadij about hiring land for gold and silver? He said: No harm. People used to hire in the time of the Prophet for watercourses and heads of streams and some crops. This would perish and that would be safe, and this would be safe and that would perish. The people had no hiring except this, so it was forbidden. As for something known and guaranteed, there is no harm. (Muslim: Chapter on hiring land for gold and silver, no. 1548). Proof: (1) The verse to establish: She must prepare the child's food... {And provide for them according to the means of the wealthy and the poor, a provision with fairness, a duty upon the doers of good} (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:236). 24. Proof: (1) Hadith to establish: If she breastfeeds him during the period with goat's milk, she has no wage... The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Muslims are bound by their conditions.' (Bukhari, Chapter on the wage of the broker, no. 2274). Proof: (1) Statement of a Tabi'i to establish: Whoever's work does not leave a trace... al-Thawri from al-Shaybani from al-Sha'bi said: 'He is liable for what he violates and there is no hire for him.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter: The hireman who transgresses, no. 14931). Proof: (2) Hadith to establish: Whoever's work does not leave a trace... The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Muslims are bound by their conditions.' (Bukhari, Chapter on the wage of the broker, no. 2274). Principle: When the work is not specified, common custom is considered. 24. Principle: If one violates the condition, he is not entitled to wage.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage from Quduri's matn on invalid lease (ijarah fasidah) covers several rulings. The first ruling (22) states that when a woman is hired as a wet nurse, the lessee (the one hiring her) cannot prevent her husband from having intercourse with her. This is because the hire does not transfer ownership of her body; she retains her marital rights. If she becomes pregnant, the lessee may cancel the lease, as pregnancy may affect her ability to nurse. The second ruling (23) obligates her to prepare the child's food, which is part of her duties. The third (24) says if she breastfeeds the child with goat's milk (i.e., not her own milk) during the lease period, she gets no wage because she is not fulfilling the contracted service. The proofs include a hadith from Rafi' ibn Khadij about hiring land, a Quranic verse on maintenance, and the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions.' The fourth ruling (25) distinguishes between craftsmen whose work leaves a physical trace on the object (like dyeing or fulling cloth) and those whose work does not (like carrying goods). The former may detain the object after work until paid, while the latter may not. This is supported by the statement of al-Sha'bi and the same hadith on conditions. Two usul principles are added: when the specific work is not mentioned, custom ('urf) is authoritative; and violating a condition forfeits the wage.

Key Terms
إجارة فاسدة (ijārah fāsidah): A lease contract that is invalid due to a defect in its essential conditions, such as uncertainty in the subject matter or wage.
أجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for similar work in the same place and time.
حبس العين (habs al-ʿayn): Detaining the physical object after completion of work until the wage is paid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following workers has the right to detain the object after completing the work?
A) A porter (حمال)
B) A boatman (ملاح)
C) A dyer (صباغ)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school differentiates between craftsmen whose work leaves a trace and those who don't for detention rights, and emphasizes that a wet nurse must fulfill contracted duties or forfeit wage.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Wage Dispute in Invalid Lease
Quduri matn with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on wage dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the wage dispute and apply the hadith on burden of proof to determine who takes oath.

Core Idea
In a wage dispute, the owner's oath prevails unless the craftsman is a regular or beginner.

This passage from Quduri presents a classic intra-Hanafi disagreement. When the owner claims the work was free and the craftsman claims wage, whose word is accepted? Abu Hanifa defaults to the owner as defendant, but his students add conditions based on the craftsman's relationship with the owner or his profession. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply evidentiary principles in contractual conflicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario and the three positions
Note the conflicting claims: owner says 'without wage', craftsman says 'with wage'. List the rulings of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
Abu Hanifa: owner's statement + oath; Abu Yusuf: if harif (regular), craftsman's claim accepted; Muhammad: if mubtadil (beginner for wage), craftsman's claim accepted.
2
Locate the common proof
Find the hadith quoted: 'al-bayyinah 'ala man idda'a wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara'. The burden of proof is on the claimant, oath on the denier.
This hadith is the foundation; the dispute is about its application.
3
Understand how each imam applies the hadith differently
Abu Hanifa sees the craftsman as claimant (seeking wage) and owner as denier, so owner takes oath. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider custom: a regular or beginning craftsman is less likely to work for free, so they shift the burden.
This is not a rejection of the hadith but a contextual interpretation.
4
Analyze the conditions introduced by the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf's condition: the craftsman is a regular (harif) of the owner. Muhammad's condition: the craftsman is a beginner in that craft for wage (mubtadil). Distinguish these concepts.
Harif implies a pattern of paid work; mubtadil implies the craftsman's known profession is wage-based.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In a court, Abu Hanifa would rule on oath alone; Abu Yusuf would investigate the relationship; Muhammad would check the craftsman's status. The mufta bihi is often Abu Hanifa's position.
Understand how the ruling changes in practice based on which imam's view is followed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْإِجَارَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ وَإِذَا شَرَطَ عَلَى الصَّانِعِ أَنْ يَعْمَلَ بِنَفْسِهِ فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَسْتَعْمِلَ غَيْرَهُ ٢٧ وَإِنْ قَالَ صَاحِبُ الثَّوْبِ عَمِلْتَهُ لِي بِغَيْرِ أُجْرَةٍ وَقَالَ الصَّانِعُ بِأَجْرَةٍ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ صَاحِبِ الثَّوْبِ مَعَ يَمِينِهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ إِنْ كَانَ حَرِيفًا لَهُ فَلَهُ الْأَجْرَةُ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ حَرِيفًا فَلَا أُجْرَةَ لَهُ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ إِنْ كَانَ الصَّانِعُ مُبْتَدِلًا هِذِهِ الصَّنْعَةِ بِالْأُجْرَةِ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ إِنَّهُ عَمِلَهُ بِأَجْرَةٍ
٢٨ وَالْوَاجِبُ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ أَجْرَةُ الْمِثْلِ لَا يَتَجَاوَزُ بِمَا الْمُسَمَّى
وجه : (١) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا شَرَطَ عَلَى الصَّانِعِ أَنْ يَعْمَلَ بِنَفْسِهِ اعَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ [؟] فِي رَجُل دَفَعَ إِلَى الْآخَرِ مَالًا مُضَارَبَةً، فَقَالَ صَاحِبُ الْمَالِ: بِالثُّلُثِ، وَقَالَ الْآخَرُ: بِالنِّصْفِ قَالَ: «الْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ صَاحِبِ الْمَالِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَأْتِي الْآخَرُ بِبَيِّنَةٍ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: اخْتِلَافُ الْمُضَارِبِينَ إِذَا ضَرَبَ بِهِ مَرَّةً أُخْرَى، نمبر 15104)
وجه:(٢) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا شَرَطَ عَلَى الصَّانِعِ أَنْ يَعْمَلَ بِنَفْسِهِ اكَتَبَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ [؟] رضي الله عنهما: «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَضَى بِالْيَمِينِ عَلَى الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ » بخاري شريف، بَابٌ: الْيَمِينُ عَلَى الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ، غمبر 2668)
٢٧ وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ صَاحِبُ الثَّوْبِ عَمِلْتَهُ لِي بِغَيْرِ أُجْرَةٍ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبِ ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، قَالَ: «الْبَيِّنَةُ عَلَى مَنِ ادَّعَى ، وَالْيَمِينُ عَلَى مَنْ أَنْكَرَ إِلَّا فِي الْقَسَامَةِ»» (سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْخُدُودِ وَالدِّيَاتِ وَغَيْرُهُ، نمبر 3191)
وجه : (١) قول التابعى لثبوت وَالْوَاجِبُ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ أُجْرَةُ الْمِثْلِ لَا يَتَجَاوَزُ بِمَا الْمُسَمَّى وَاكْتَرَى الْحَسَنُ مِنْ عَبْدِ اللهِ بْنِ مِرْدَاسِ حِمَارًا فَقَالَ بِكُمْ قَالَ بِدَانَقَيْنِ فَرَكِبَهُ ثُمَّ جَاءَ مَرَّةً أُخْرَى فَقَالَ الْحِمَارَ الْحِمَارَ فَرَكِبَهُ وَلَمْ يُشَارِطْهُ فَبَعَثَ إِلَيْهِ بِنِصْفِ دِرْهَمٍ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ أَجْرَى أَمْرَ الْأَمْصَارِ عَلَى مَا يَتَعَارَفُونَ بَيْنَهُمْ فِي الْبُيُوعِ وَالإِجَارَةِ، نمبر (2210)
وجه:(٢) الآية الثبوت وَالْوَاجِبُ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ أُجْرَةُ الْمِثْلِ لَا يَتَجَاوَزُ بِمَا الْمُسَمَّى ال﴿وَمَن كَانَ غَنِيًّا فَلْيَسْتَعْفِفْ وَمَن كَانَ فَقِيرًا فَلْيَأْكُلْ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ فَإِذَا دَفَعْتُمْ إِلَيْهِمْ أَمْوَلَهُمْ فَأَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِمْ وَكَفَى بِاللَّهِ حَسِيبًا) (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر 6)
٢٦ اصول: کاریگر کاریگر میں مہارت اور تجربہ کا فرق ہوتا ہے، اسی کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔
Chapter of Invalid Lease. And if he stipulated upon the craftsman that he work himself, then he may not employ another. 27. And if the owner of the cloth says, 'You did it for me without wage,' and the craftsman says, 'With wage,' then the statement is the statement of the owner of the cloth with his oath according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: If he is his regular customer (harif), then he gets the wage; if not, then no wage. Muhammad said: If the craftsman is a beginner (mubtadil) in this craft for wage, then his statement is accepted that he did it for wage. 28. And the obligatory (payment) in an invalid lease is the fair wage (ujrat al-mithl), not exceeding the agreed wage. Proof: (1) Statement of a Tabi'i to establish: And if he stipulated... from al-Thawri concerning a man who gave another capital for mudarabah; the owner said 'for a third' and the other said 'for a half'; he said: 'The statement is the statement of the owner unless the other brings evidence.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter: Disagreement of mudaribun, no. 15104). Proof: (2) Hadith to establish: And if he stipulated... Ibn Abbas wrote that the Prophet ﷺ judged that the oath is upon the defendant. (Bukhari, Chapter: Oath upon the defendant, no. 2668). 27. Proof: (1) Hadith to establish: And if the owner says... from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the one who denies, except in cases of qasama.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Book of Hudud and Diyat, no. 3191). Proof: (1) Statement of a Tabi'i to establish: And the obligatory payment in invalid lease is the fair wage not exceeding... al-Hasan hired a donkey from Abdullah ibn Mirdas and said 'for how much?' He said 'for two daniqs.' He rode it, then came another time and said 'the donkey, the donkey' and rode it without bargaining, and sent him half a dirham. (Bukhari, Chapter: Who conducts the affairs of cities according to custom, no. 2210). Proof: (2) The verse to establish: And the obligatory payment in invalid lease is the fair wage not exceeding... {And whoever is rich, let him abstain; and whoever is poor, let him eat in fairness. And when you give them their wealth, take witnesses over them, and sufficient is Allah as a Reckoner} (Surah al-Nisa, 4:6). 26. Principle: There is a difference among craftsmen in skill and experience; that is taken into account.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage from the same chapter continues with two major rulings and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The first ruling (27) states that if the employer stipulated that the craftsman work personally, he cannot delegate the work to another. This is proven by a statement of al-Thawri (a Tabi'i) and the hadith that the oath is on the defendant. The second ruling involves a dispute between the owner of the cloth and the craftsman about whether the work was for wage or free. Abu Hanifa holds that the owner's statement with his oath is accepted because he is the defendant (the craftsman is claiming extra payment). Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if the craftsman is a regular customer (harif) of the owner, meaning he usually works for him for wage, then the craftsman's claim is accepted; otherwise the owner's word prevails. Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani says: if the craftsman is a beginner in this trade specifically for wage (i.e., he is known to take wage for such work), then his statement that it was for wage is accepted. The basis is the hadith 'al-bayyinah 'ala man idda'a' (the burden of proof is on the claimant). The owner is denying the wage claim, so he is the defendant. The final ruling (28) states that in an invalid lease (where the contract is fasid), the obligatory payment is the fair wage (ujrat al-mithl), but it cannot exceed the agreed wage if one was specified. Proofs include the practice of al-Hasan al-Basri (Tabi'i) and a Quranic verse. An usul principle adds that the skill and experience of the craftsman matter when determining the fair wage.

Key Terms
حريف (ḥarīf): A regular customer or associate who customarily works with or for someone on a wage basis.
مبتدل (mubtadil): A beginner or one who undertakes a craft for wage; according to Muhammad, such a person's claim of wage is accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, in a dispute where the owner says the work was free and the craftsman says it was for wage, whose statement is accepted?
A) The craftsman, because he is the worker
B) The owner, with his oath
C) The craftsman, with his oath
D) Both take an oath and nothing is paid

Key Takeaway
In a wage dispute, the owner's oath prevails unless the craftsman is a regular (harif) or beginner (mubtadil), depending on which Hanafi authority is followed.

Obligation of Ujrat al-Mithl in Invalid Lease
Quduri matn with ruling on ujrat al-mithl in invalid lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that ujrat al-mithl is wajib in an invalid lease and identify the Hanafi condition that it cannot exceed the named wage.

Core Idea
Fair wage for invalid lease is wajib, but capped at the agreed wage.

This passage addresses the financial consequence when a lease contract is invalid (fasid). Even though the contract is not valid, the worker is entitled to a fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) for work performed. However, if a wage was named in the contract, the fair wage cannot exceed that amount. This ruling prevents the worker from gaining more than originally agreed, balancing fairness with contractual limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states: 'And the obligatory in invalid lease is the fair wage, not exceeding the named wage.' Note that the lease is invalid, so the named wage is not binding, but it serves as a cap.
Invalid lease means the contract has a defect that prevents it from being sahih, but the work was already done.
2
Understand ujrat al-mithl
Ujrat al-mithl is the market rate for similar work in the same place and time. Factors include skill, experience, and location.
The commentary mentions a principle: 'There is a difference among craftsmen in skill and experience; that is taken into account.'
3
Examine the proofs
The passage provides two proofs: (1) The practice of al-Hasan al-Basri, who voluntarily paid half a dirham for riding a donkey without a fixed wage, indicating ujrat al-mithl. (2) The Quranic verse (4:6) on paying in fairness.
The verse is about guardians of orphans, but its general principle of 'in fairness' supports ujrat al-mithl.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school caps the fair wage at the named wage. The Shafi'i school does not impose this cap; the worker may claim full ujrat al-mithl even if it exceeds the named wage.
This difference arises from whether the named wage, though in an invalid contract, still establishes a limit.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Example: A man hires a carpenter to build a cupboard for 100 dirhams, but the contract is invalid because the carpenter was required to work himself but subcontracted. The carpenter finishes the work. The fair wage is 150 dirhams. Hanafi: the carpenter gets only 100 dirhams (the named wage). Shafi'i: he gets 150.
Practice this distinction.

Source Text

٢٨ وَالْوَاجِبُ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ أَجْرَةُ الْمِثْلِ لَا يَتَجَاوَزُ بِمَا الْمُسَمَّى
وجه : (١) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا شَرَطَ عَلَى الصَّانِعِ أَنْ يَعْمَلَ بِنَفْسِهِ اعَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ [؟] فِي رَجُل دَفَعَ إِلَى الْآخَرِ مَالًا مُضَارَبَةً، فَقَالَ صَاحِبُ الْمَالِ: بِالثُّلُثِ، وَقَالَ الْآخَرُ: بِالنِّصْفِ قَالَ: «الْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ صَاحِبِ الْمَالِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَأْتِي الْآخَرُ بِبَيِّنَةٍ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: اخْتِلَافُ الْمُضَارِبِينَ إِذَا ضَرَبَ بِهِ مَرَّةً أُخْرَى، نمبر 15104)
وجه:(٢) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا شَرَطَ عَلَى الصَّانِعِ أَنْ يَعْمَلَ بِنَفْسِهِ اكَتَبَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ [؟] رضي الله عنهما: «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَضَى بِالْيَمِينِ عَلَى الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ » بخاري شريف، بَابٌ: الْيَمِينُ عَلَى الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ، غمبر 2668)
٢٧ وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ صَاحِبُ الثَّوْبِ عَمِلْتَهُ لِي بِغَيْرِ أُجْرَةٍ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبِ ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، قَالَ: «الْبَيِّنَةُ عَلَى مَنِ ادَّعَى ، وَالْيَمِينُ عَلَى مَنْ أَنْكَرَ إِلَّا فِي الْقَسَامَةِ»» (سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْخُدُودِ وَالدِّيَاتِ وَغَيْرُهُ، نمبر 3191)
وجه : (١) قول التابعى لثبوت وَالْوَاجِبُ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ أُجْرَةُ الْمِثْلِ لَا يَتَجَاوَزُ بِمَا الْمُسَمَّى وَاكْتَرَى الْحَسَنُ مِنْ عَبْدِ اللهِ بْنِ مِرْدَاسِ حِمَارًا فَقَالَ بِكُمْ قَالَ بِدَانَقَيْنِ فَرَكِبَهُ ثُمَّ جَاءَ مَرَّةً أُخْرَى فَقَالَ الْحِمَارَ الْحِمَارَ فَرَكِبَهُ وَلَمْ يُشَارِطْهُ فَبَعَثَ إِلَيْهِ بِنِصْفِ دِرْهَمٍ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ أَجْرَى أَمْرَ الْأَمْصَارِ عَلَى مَا يَتَعَارَفُونَ بَيْنَهُمْ فِي الْبُيُوعِ وَالإِجَارَةِ، نمبر (2210)
وجه:(٢) الآية الثبوت وَالْوَاجِبُ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ أُجْرَةُ الْمِثْلِ لَا يَتَجَاوَزُ بِمَا الْمُسَمَّى ال﴿وَمَن كَانَ غَنِيًّا فَلْيَسْتَعْفِفْ وَمَن كَانَ فَقِيرًا فَلْيَأْكُلْ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ فَإِذَا دَفَعْتُمْ إِلَيْهِمْ أَمْوَلَهُمْ فَأَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِمْ وَكَفَى بِاللَّهِ حَسِيبًا) (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر 6)

Chapter of Invalid Lease. And if he stipulated upon the craftsman that he work himself, then he may not employ another. 27. And if the owner of the cloth says, 'You did it for me without wage,' and the craftsman says, 'With wage,' then the statement is the statement of the owner of the cloth with his oath according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: If he is his regular customer (harif), then he gets the wage; if not, then no wage. Muhammad said: If the craftsman is a beginner (mubtadil) in this craft for wage, then his statement is accepted that he did it for wage. 28. And the obligatory (payment) in an invalid lease is the fair wage (ujrat al-mithl), not exceeding the agreed wage. Proof: (1) Statement of a Tabi'i to establish: And if he stipulated... from al-Thawri concerning a man who gave another capital for mudarabah; the owner said 'for a third' and the other said 'for a half'; he said: 'The statement is the statement of the owner unless the other brings evidence.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter: Disagreement of mudaribun, no. 15104). Proof: (2) Hadith to establish: And if he stipulated... Ibn Abbas wrote that the Prophet ﷺ judged that the oath is upon the defendant. (Bukhari, Chapter: Oath upon the defendant, no. 2668). 27. Proof: (1) Hadith to establish: And if the owner says... from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the one who denies, except in cases of qasama.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Book of Hudud and Diyat, no. 3191). Proof: (1) Statement of a Tabi'i to establish: And the obligatory payment in invalid lease is the fair wage not exceeding... al-Hasan hired a donkey from Abdullah ibn Mirdas and said 'for how much?' He said 'for two daniqs.' He rode it, then came another time and said 'the donkey, the donkey' and rode it without bargaining, and sent him half a dirham. (Bukhari, Chapter: Who conducts the affairs of cities according to custom, no. 2210). Proof: (2) The verse to establish: And the obligatory payment in invalid lease is the fair wage not exceeding... {And whoever is rich, let him abstain; and whoever is poor, let him eat in fairness. And when you give them their wealth, take witnesses over them, and sufficient is Allah as a Reckoner} (Surah al-Nisa, 4:6). 26. Principle: There is a difference among craftsmen in skill and experience; that is taken into account.

Commentary
This passage from the same chapter continues with two major rulings and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The first ruling (27) states that if the employer stipulated that the craftsman work personally, he cannot delegate the work to another. This is proven by a statement of al-Thawri (a Tabi'i) and the hadith that the oath is on the defendant. The second ruling involves a dispute between the owner of the cloth and the craftsman about whether the work was for wage or free. Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if the craftsman is a regular customer (harif) of the owner, meaning he usually works for him for wage, then the craftsman's claim is accepted; otherwise the owner's word prevails. The basis is the hadith 'al-bayyinah 'ala man idda'a' (the burden of proof is on the claimant). The owner is denying the wage claim, so he is the defendant. The final ruling (28) states that in an invalid lease (where the contract is fasid), the obligatory payment is the fair wage (ujrat al-mithl), but it cannot exceed the agreed wage if one was specified. Key Terms
أجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for similar work in the same context; obligatory in invalid lease but capped at the agreed wage if any.

Checkpoint
In an invalid lease contract where a named wage of 100 dirhams was agreed and the fair wage is 150 dirhams, how much must the hirer pay according to the Hanafi school?
A) 0 dirhams, because the contract is invalid
B) 150 dirhams, the fair wage

Obligation of Pre-emption for Co-owner and Neighbor
Proving pre-emption right for co-owner, then right-holder, then neighbor with scriptural evidence and a madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shuf'ah (pre-emption) for the three categories of right-holders and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
Pre-emption is wajib for co-owner in property, then co-owner in rights, then neighbor; the Hanafis uphold neighbor's pre-emption even after division.

This lesson opens the Book of Pre-emption (shuf'ah) by stating the Hanafi position on who has the right of pre-emption and in what order. The author then adduces several hadith to support the ruling and finally presents the evidence of Imam al-Shafi'i, who restricts pre-emption to co-owners in undivided property. Understanding this lesson will equip you to identify the three classes of pre-emptors and appreciate the scriptural basis for the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its hukm level
The text begins with 'al-shuf‘atu wājibatun' – pre-emption is obligatory. Note that wājib is a Hanafi level between fard and sunnah, established by zanni evidence.
The ruling is not fard because the proofs are ahad hadith, which give zanni certainty.
2
List the three categories of pre-emptors in order
First priority: the co-owner in the very property (khalīṭ fī nafs al-mabī‘). Second: the co-owner in a right appurtenant to the property, such as a water share or path. Third: the neighbor (jār).
Each category has a lower priority than the one before it.
3
Examine the hadith proofs and their points of evidence
Multiple hadith are cited: 'al-jāru aḥaqqu bi saqabihī', 'al-shafī‘u awlā min al-jār', and the hadith of Jabir about informing a partner. Identify how each phrase supports the right of pre-emption.
The Hanafis use these as general proofs that pre-emption applies to neighbors as well.
4
Note the Shafi'i counter-evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith of Jabir ibn ‘Abdullah: 'The Messenger of Allah gave judgment of shuf‘ah in everything that has not been divided; but when boundaries are fixed and roads are made, there is no shuf‘ah.'
This hadith appears to limit pre-emption to undivided property.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis interpret the Shafi'i hadith as applying to pre-emption for rights of way or water shares, not to negate neighbor's pre-emption. They argue that a specific hadith cannot abrogate general ones without clear indication, and the general hadith supporting neighbor's pre-emption are preferred.
Thus, the Hanafi position remains mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الشُّفْعَةِ
قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ: الشُّفْعَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ، ثُمَّ الْخَلِيطِ فِي حَقِّ الْمَبِيعِ كَالشُّرْبِ وَالطَّرِيقِ، ثُمَّ لِلْجَارِ.
وَجْهُ (١) الْحَدِيثِ لِثُبُوتِ الشُّفْعَةِ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ: سَمِعَ أَبَا رَافِعٍ، سَمِعَ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «الْجَارُ أَحَقُّ بِسَقَبِهِ» (سنن أبي داود، باب في الشفعة، رقم 3516)
وَجْهُ (١) الْحَدِيثِ لِثُبُوتِ الشُّفْعَةِ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ: سَمِعْتُ الشَّعْبِيَّ يَقُولُ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «الشَّفِيعُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْجَارِ، وَالْجَارُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْجَنُبِ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الشفعة بالجوار، والخليط أحق، رقم 14390 / مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من كان يقضي بالشفعة للجار، رقم 22717)
وَجْهُ (١) قَوْلِ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ الشُّفْعَةِ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ: عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: الْخَلِيطُ أَحَقُّ مِنَ الْجَارِ، وَالْجَارُ أَحَقُّ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الشفعة بالجوار، والخليط أحق، رقم 14389)
وَجْهُ (٢) الْحَدِيثِ لِثُبُوتِ الشُّفْعَةِ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ: عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ شَرِيكٌ فِي رَبْعَةٍ أَوْ نَخْلٍ، فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَبِيعَ حَتَّى يُؤْذِنَ شَرِيكَهُ، فَإِنْ رَضِيَ أَخَذَ، وَإِنْ كَرِهَ تَرَكَ» (مسلم، باب الشفعة، رقم 1608 / أبو داود، باب في الشفعة، رقم 3513)
وَجْهُ (٣) الْحَدِيثِ لِثُبُوتِ الشُّفْعَةِ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ: عَنْ سَمُرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «جَارُ الدَّارِ أَحَقُّ بِدَارِ الْجَارِ أَوِ الْأَرْضِ» (سنن أبي داود، باب في الشفعة، رقم 3517 / سنن الترمذي، باب ما جاء في الشفعة، رقم 1368)
وَجْهُ (١) دَلِيلِ الشَّافِعِيِّ: حَدِيثُ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: «قَضَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِالشُّفْعَةِ فِي كُلِّ مَا لَمْ يُقْسَمْ، فَإِذَا وَقَعَتِ الْحُدُودُ وَصُرِفَتِ الطُّرُقُ فَلَا شُفْعَةَ» (البخاري، كتاب الشفعة، باب الشفعة ما لم يقسم...، رقم 2257)
أصول: شفعہ کسی کی غیر منقولی جائداد یا زمین میں لینے میں اس کے پڑوسی کو دوسرے کے مقابل حق ہوتا ہے۔
Book of Pre-emption. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: Pre-emption is obligatory for the co-owner in the very object of sale, then the co-owner in a right of the object of sale such as water share and path, then for the neighbor. Proof (1) hadith for establishing that pre-emption is obligatory for the co-owner in the very object of sale: Abu Rafi‘ heard the Prophet say: 'The neighbor is more entitled to his adjacent property.' Proof (1) hadith: I heard al-Sha‘bi say: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The co-sharer is more entitled than the neighbor, and the neighbor is more entitled than a stranger.' Proof (1) saying of a follower: from Ibrahim who said: 'The co-sharer is more entitled than the neighbor, and the neighbor is more entitled than others.' Proof (2) hadith: from Jabir who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever has a partner in a dwelling or a palm tree, he may not sell until he informs his partner; if he is pleased, he takes, and if he dislikes, he leaves.' Proof (3) hadith: from Samurah from the Prophet who said: 'The neighbor of a house is more entitled to the house of the neighbor or land.' Proof (1) of al-Shafi‘i: the hadith of Jabir ibn ‘Abdullah who said: 'The Messenger of Allah gave judgment of pre-emption in everything that has not been divided; but when boundaries are fixed and roads are made, there is no pre-emption.' Principle: Pre-emption gives a neighbor the right to take another's immovable property or land in preference to others.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Pre-emption (shuf‘ah). The author states the Hanafi position: shuf‘ah is obligatory (wājib) for three categories in order of priority: first, the co-owner (khalīṭ) in the same property (i.e., an undivided share); second, the co-owner in a right pertaining to the property, such as a water share (shurb) or a right of way (ṭarīq); third, the neighbor (jār). The ruling is supported by multiple hadith and a saying of the tabi‘i Ibrahim al-Nakha‘i. The hadith include: 'The neighbor is more entitled to his adjacent property' (Abu Dawud), 'The co-sharer is more entitled than the neighbor, and the neighbor more than a stranger' (Ibn Abi Shaybah), and 'Whoever has a partner... must inform him' (Muslim). Then the author presents the proof of al-Shafi‘i: the hadith of Jabir that pre-emption only applies before division; after boundaries and roads are fixed, there is no pre-emption. This indicates a difference of opinion between the Hanafis and Shafi‘is: Hanafis extend pre-emption to neighbors even after division, while Shafi‘is limit it to co-owners in undivided property. The usul note in Urdu summarizes that pre-emption gives a neighbor a preferential right to purchase.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf‘ah): Pre-emption: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to take over the property that is being sold, by paying the price, in preference to an outsider.
الخليط (al-khalīṭ): Co-owner or partner in the same property or in a right appurtenant to the property (like water share or path). The first category is the co-owner in the property itself; the second is the co-owner in a right.
الجار (al-jār): Neighbor: the owner of an adjacent property. In the context of shuf‘ah, the neighbor has a right of pre-emption after the co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in the passage, who has the first priority right of pre-emption (shuf‘ah)?
A) The neighbor
B) The co-owner in the property itself
C) The co-owner in a right like water share
D) Any stranger

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, shuf'ah is wājib for three classes in hierarchical order: co-owner in property, co-owner in rights, then neighbor; the neighbor's right persists even after the land is divided.

The Hierarchy of Preemption Rights and Their Stages
Establishes the legal order of preemption holders and the stages of the preemption right.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of preemptors in order and explain the three stages of the preemption right (obligation, establishment, ownership).

Core Idea
Preemption belongs first to the co-owner in the property, then to co-owners in rights, then to the neighbor.

In this passage from Al-Quduri's matn, the Hanafi school lays out the foundational rules of shuf'ah (preemption). You will learn the precise hierarchy of who has the right to preempt a sold property and the temporal phases through which that right matures. The passage also provides the hadith proofs that ground these rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its legal weight
Identify that shuf'ah is wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school. Note why it is not fard: the proofs are ahad (zanni thubut).
The hukm level is important because it determines the consequence of omission – leaving shuf'ah without a valid excuse is sinful.
2
Identify the three categories of preemptors
From the text: first, the khalit fi nafs al-mabi' (co-owner in the property itself); second, the khalit fi haqq al-mabi' (co-owner in rights like water and pathway); third, the jar (neighbor).
The order is sequential: the next claimant only gets the right if the previous one relinquishes.
3
Explain the rule for co-owners in pathway/water and neighbor
The text explicitly says that a mere co-owner in pathway or water has no preemption against the co-owner in the property. The neighbor's right is only after the co-owner in rights waives.
This establishes a strict priority; the neighbor cannot claim if any co-owner (in property or rights) still wants the property.
4
Describe the three stages of the preemption right
The passage states: (1) wujub (obligation) arises with the contract of sale; (2) istiqrar (establishment) occurs with witnessing/claiming; (3) milk (ownership) is attained by taking possession (akhdh) with the buyer's consent or a judge's ruling.
If the preemptor delays claiming, the right may be lost – as implied by the hadith 'shuf'ah is like loosening the hobble' (must act quickly).
5
Analyze the proofs cited
The passage provides multiple hadith and sayings of the Salaf to support each ruling. Most notably, the hadith 'The neighbor has more right to his adjacent property' is used for the neighbor's right, while the Shafi'i hadith 'Preemption is only in undivided property' is also cited, showing the ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi approach reconciles these texts by ranking the hadith of the neighbor as general and the undivided property hadith as specific to co-ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الشُّفْعَةِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ -: الشُّفْعَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ ثُمَّ الْخَلِيطُ فِي حَقِّ الْمَبِيعِ كَالشُّرْبِ وَالطَّرِيقِ ثُمَّ لِلْجَارِ.
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت الشُّفْعَةِ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ: سَمِعَ أَبَا رَافِعٍ، سَمِعَ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «الْجَارُ أَحَقُّ بِسَقَبِهِ» (سنن أبي داود، باب الشفعة، رقم 3516). وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت الشُّفْعَةِ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ: سَمِعْتُ الشَّعْبِيَّ يَقُولُ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الشَّفِيعُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْجَارِ، وَالْجَارُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْجُنُبِ»، (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الشفعة بالجوار، والخليط أحق، رقم 14390/ مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من كان يقضي بالشفعة للجار، رقم 22717). وجه (١) قول التابعي لثبوت الشُّفْعَةِ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ: عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «الخليط أحق من الجار، والجار أحق من غيره» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الشفعة بالجوار، والخليط أحق، رقم 14389). وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت الشُّفْعَةِ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ: عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ شَرِيكٌ فِي رَبْعَةٍ أَوْ نَخْلٍ، فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَبِيعَ حَتَّى يُؤْذِنَ شَرِيكَهُ، فَإِنْ رَضِيَ أَخَذَ، وَإِنْ كَرِهَ تَرَكَ» (مسلم، باب الشفعة، رقم 1608/ أبو داود، باب الشفعة، 3513). وجه (٣) الحديث لثبوت الشُّفْعَةِ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ: عَنْ سَمُرَةَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «جَارُ الدَّارِ أَحَقُّ بِدَارِ الْجَارِ أَوِ الْأَرْضِ» (سنن أبي داود، باب الشفعة، رقم 3517/ سنن الترمذي، باب ما جاء في الشفعة، رقم 1368). وجه (١) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت الشُّفْعَةِ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلْخَلِيطِ فِي نَفْسِ الْمَبِيعِ: عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: «قَضَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالشُّفْعَةِ فِي كُلِّ مَا لَمْ يُقْسَمْ، فَإِذَا وَقَعَتِ الْحُدُودُ وَصُرِفَتِ الطُّرُقُ فَلَا شُفْعَةَ» (البخاري، كتاب الشفعة، باب: الشفعة ما لم يقسم، فإذا وقعت الحدود فلا شفعة، رقم 2257). 
أصول: شفعہ کسی کی غیر منقولی جائداد یا زمین میں اس کے پڑوسی کو دوسرے کے مقابل حق ہوتا ہے۔
وَلَيْسَ لِلشَّرِيكِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ وَالشُّرْبِ، وَالْجَارِ شُفْعَةٌ مَعَ الْخَلِيطِ، فَإِنْ سَلَّمَ فَالشُّفْعَةُ لِلشَّرِيكِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ، فَإِنْ سَلَّمَ أَخَذَهَا الْجَارُ، وَالشُّفْعَةُ تَجِبُ بِعَقْدِ الْبَيْعِ وَتَسْتَقِرُّ بِالْإِشْهَادِ وَتُمْلَكُ بِالْأَخْذِ إِذَا سَلَّمَهَا الْمُشْتَرِي، أَوْ حَكَمَ بِمَا حَاكِمٌ.
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ لِلشَّرِيكِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ وَالشُّرْبِ: سَمِعْتُ الشَّعْبِيَّ يَقُولُ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الشَّفِيعُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْجَارِ، وَالْجَارُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْجُنُبِ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الشفعة بالجوار، والخليط أحق، رقم 14390/ مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من كان يقضي بالشفعة للجار، رقم 22717). وجه (٢) قول التابعي لثبوت وَلَيْسَ لِلشَّرِيكِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ وَالشُّرْبِ: عَنْ شُرَيْحٍ قَالَ: «الْخَلِيطُ أَحَقُّ مِنَ الشَّفِيعِ، وَالشَّفِيعُ أَحَقُّ مِنَ الْجَارِ، وَالْجَارُ أَحَقُّ مِمَّنْ سِوَاهُ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من كان يقضي بالشفعة للجار، رقم 22725/ مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الشفعة بالجوار، والخليط أحق، رقم 14389). وجه (١) قول التابعي لثبوت وَالشُّفْعَةُ تَجِبُ بِعَقْدِ الْبَيْعِ وَتَسْتَقِرُّ بِالْإِشْهَادِ: وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي لَيْلَى: «لا يَقَعُ لَهُ شُفْعَةٌ حَتَّى يَقَعَ الْبَيْعُ، فَإِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب: الشفيع يأذن قبل البيع، وكم وقتها، رقم 14404). وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَالشُّفْعَةُ تَجِبُ بِعَقْدِ الْبَيْعِ وَتَسْتَقِرُّ بِالْإِشْهَادِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الشُّفْعَةُ كَحَلِّ الْعِقَالِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، باب طلب الشفعة، رقم 2500/ السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب رواية ألفاظ منكرة يذكرها بعض الفقهاء في مسائل الشفعة، رقم 11589). وجه (٣) قول التابعي لثبوت وَالشُّفْعَةُ تَجِبُ بِعَقْدِ الْبَيْعِ وَتَسْتَقِرُّ بِالْإِشْهَادِ: وَقَالَ الشَّعْبِيُّ: «مَنْ بِيعَتْ شُفْعَتُهُ وَهُوَ شَاهِدٌ لَا يُغَيِّرُهَا فَلَا شُفْعَةَ لَهُ» (البخاري، باب عرض الشفعة على صاحبها قبل البيع، رقم 2258/ مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الشفيع يأذن قبل البيع، وكم وقتها، رقم 14405).
أصول: جب بائع مبیع کو اپنی ملکیت سے نکالنے کا ارادہ کرے تب شفیع کو حق شفعہ ہو گا، اس سے قبل نہیں۔
The Book of Preemption. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him -: Preemption is obligatory for the co-owner in the property itself, then the co-owner in the right of the property like water share and pathway, then for the neighbor. Aspect (1) of the hadith for establishing that preemption is obligatory for the co-owner in the property itself: ... (various hadith and statements are cited) ... And the co-owner in the pathway and water share has no preemption, and the neighbor has preemption with the co-owner; if he (the co-owner) relinquishes, then preemption is for the co-owner in the pathway; if he relinquishes, the neighbor takes it. And preemption becomes obligatory by the contract of sale, becomes established by witnessing, and is owned by taking delivery if the buyer hands it over, or if a judge so rules. Aspect (1) ... (various proofs follow) ... Principles: Preemption is a right for the neighbor over others in someone's immovable property or land. (Urdu) Principles: When the seller intends to remove the sold item from his ownership, then the preemptor has the right of preemption, not before.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn begins the Book of Preemption (Shuf'ah). It is a ruling statement with multiple proofs (hadith and sayings of the Salaf). The passage first states the general ruling: preemption is obligatory (wajib) for three categories in order of priority: (1) the co-owner (khalit) in the actual property being sold (e.g., joint ownership in land), (2) the co-owner in the rights pertaining to the property, such as a shared water channel (shurb) or a common pathway (tariq), and (3) the neighbor (jar) who is adjacent to the property. The text then specifies that a mere co-owner in a pathway or water channel (without being a co-owner in the property itself) does not have preemption; rather, the co-owner in the property has the primary right. If the co-owner in the property relinquishes his right, then the co-owner in the pathway/water gets it, and if that one relinquishes, the neighbor takes it. The passage also clarifies the stages of the preemption right: it becomes wajib (obligatory) upon the conclusion of the sale contract, it becomes firmly established (mustaqirr) by the witnesses being present (i.e., the preemptor must claim immediately), and it is owned (tamalluk) by actually taking possession (akhdh) when the buyer voluntarily hands over the property or a judge orders its transfer. The passage then provides numerous hadith and statements from the Salaf (including the famous hadith 'The neighbor has more right to his adjacent property' and 'Preemption is like loosening the hobble' meaning it must be acted upon quickly) as proofs for these rulings. The Urdu principles (usul) at the end summarize: shuf'ah is a right of the neighbor over others in immovable property, and the right arises only when the seller intends to remove the property from his ownership through a sale.

Key Terms
الشُّفْعَة (al-shuf'ah): The right of a co-owner or neighbor to preempt (buy) a sold property by taking it from the buyer at the sale price.
الخَلِيط (al-khalit): A co-owner in the property itself, or in its rights (shurb, tariq).
الشَّرْب (al-shurb): The right to water for irrigation, often shared among neighbors.
الطَّرِيق (al-tariq): A pathway used to access the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, who has the first right of preemption (shuf'ah)?
A) The neighbor who lives next door.
B) The co-owner in the pathway or water share.
C) The co-owner in the property itself (khalit fi nafs al-mabi').
D) Any relative of the seller.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, preemption is a wajib right that follows a strict hierarchy: co-owner in the property, co-owner in rights, then neighbor, and it must be claimed promptly upon knowledge of the sale.

The Priority of Pre-emptors in Shuf'ah
Priority order of pre-emptors in shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of pre-emptors in shuf'ah and apply it to determine who has the right of pre-emption.

Core Idea
In Hanafi shuf'ah, the khaliṭ (co-owner in the property) has the strongest right, then the partner in road/water, then the neighbour.

Shuf'ah (pre-emption) is the right of an existing co-owner or neighbour to purchase a sold share to prevent a stranger from entering the property. The Hanafi school establishes a clear hierarchy of who is most entitled. This lesson examines the primary text from al-Quduri and its supporting proofs to understand this ranking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Listen to the Arabic text: it names three parties: the khaliṭ (mixed partner in the property itself), the sharīk fī al-ṭarīq wa al-shurb (partner in right of way and water), and the jār (neighbour). Distinguish them carefully.
The khaliṭ is the one who actually co-owns the land or building, not just easements.
2
Understand the priority order
The matn states that if the khaliṭ does not claim, then the partner in road/water gets the right; if that partner also does not claim, then the neighbour gets it. Thus the order is: first khaliṭ, then sharīk fī al-ṭarīq wa al-shurb, then jār.
3
Examine the first proof: hadith
The text cites a hadith from al-Sha'bi: 'The pre-emptor (shafi') has more right than the neighbour, and the neighbour has more right than the stranger.' Here 'shafi'' refers to the khaliṭ. This establishes the relative priority of khaliṭ over neighbour.
The hadith is transmitted as mursal but accepted by Hanafis as evidence for shuf'ah.
4
Examine the second proof: saying of Shurayh
Shurayh, a famous judge, said: 'The khaliṭ is more entitled than the shafi' (partner in road/water), and the shafi' is more entitled than the neighbour, and the neighbour is more entitled than anyone else.' This confirms the three-tier ranking.
Note: In Shurayh's wording, 'shafi'' is used for the partner in road/water, not the khaliṭ. This slight terminological difference does not affect the ruling.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position differs from the Shafi'i school, which may not distinguish between types of partners. In Shafi'i fiqh, all co-owners have a right of shuf'ah equally, and the neighbour's right is also recognized but often weaker.
Knowing this ikhtilaf helps in understanding why Hanafi fiqh specifies a detailed hierarchy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ لِلشَّرِيكِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ وَالشَّرْبِ، وَالجَارِ شُفْعَةٌ مَعَ الْخَلِيطِ فَإِنْ سَلَّمَ فَالشُّفْعَةُ لِلشَّرِيكِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ فَإِنْ سَلَّمَ أَخَذَهَا الْجَارُ
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ لِلشَّرِيكِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ وَالشَّرْبِ \ سَمِعْتُ الشَّعْبِيَّ يَقُولُ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الشَّفِيعُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْجَارِ، وَالْجَارُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْجُنُبِ»،(مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ : السُّفْعَةُ بِالْجَوَارِ، وَالخَلِيطُ أَحَقٌّ، نمبر 14390 /مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ كَانَ يَقْضِي بِالشُّفْعَةِ لِلْجَار، غمبر 22717)
وجه :(۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَيْسَ لِلشَّرِيكِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ وَالشَّرْبِ اعَنْ شُرَيْحٍ، قَالَ: «الْخَلِيطُ أَحَقُّ مِنَ الشَّفِيعِ، وَالشَّفِيعُ أَحَقُّ مِنَ الْجَارِ، وَالْجَارُ أَحَقُّ مِمَّنْ سِوَاهُ»(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ كَانَ يَقْضِي بِالشُّفْعَةِ لِلْجَارِ ، نمبر 22725/ مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ : التَّفْعَةُ بِالْجَوَارِ، وَالْخَلِيطُ أَحَقٌّ، غمبر 14389)
And there is no shuf'ah for the partner in the road and the water, and the neighbour, with the mixed partner. If he (the mixed partner) relinquishes, then the shuf'ah is for the partner in the road. Then if he relinquishes, the neighbour takes it. Proof (1) The hadith for establishing that there is no shuf'ah for the partner in the road and the water: I heard al-Sha'bi say: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'The pre-emptor (shafi') has more right than the neighbour, and the neighbour has more right than the stranger.' Proof (2) The saying of the tabi'i for establishing that there is no shuf'ah for the partner in the road and the water: From Shurayh, he said: 'The mixed partner is more entitled than the pre-emptor, and the pre-emptor is more entitled than the neighbour, and the neighbour is more entitled than anyone else.'
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage states the priority order of pre-emptors. The most entitled is the khaliṭ (mixed partner in the property itself). If he does not claim, then the partner in road and water rights (sharik fi al-tariq wa al-sharb). If he also does not claim, then the neighbour (jar) gets the right. The proofs include a hadith from al-Sha'bi reporting that the shafi' (here meaning the khaliṭ) is more entitled than the neighbour, and the neighbour more than a stranger. Also the saying of Shurayh: the khaliṭ is more entitled than the shafi' (the partner), actually the text says: 'al-khalitu ahaqqu min al-shafi'i, wa al-shafi'u ahaqqu min al-jari, wa al-jaru ahaqqu mimman siwah.' So Shurayh's opinion matches. Note: In Hanafi fiqh, the order is: 1. Khaliṭ (partner in the property itself, i.e., share of the land). 2. Sharik fi tariq wa sharb (partner in road and water rights only, not in the property). 3. Jar (adjacent neighbour). This is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
شُفْعَة (shuf'ah): The right of a co-owner to purchase the share of a new buyer in a property to prevent the entry of a stranger.
خَلِيط (khalīṭ): A person who shares ownership in the actual property (e.g., land, house) with the seller.
شَرِيك فِي الطَّرِيق وَالشَّرْب (sharīk fī al-ṭarīq wa al-shurb): A person who has a right of way (tariq) or right of water (shurb) shared with the seller, but does not own a share in the property itself.
جَار (jār): An adjacent neighbour whose property borders the sold property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is the first in priority to claim shuf'ah?
A) The partner in road and water
B) The neighbour
C) The mixed partner (khaliṭ)
D) Any co-owner

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi shuf'ah, the khaliṭ (co-owner in the property) has the strongest right, followed by the partner in easements, and lastly the neighbour.

The Three Stages of Shuf'ah: Obligation, Establishment, and Ownership
Defines the stages of shuf'ah: obligation, establishment, and ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three stages of shuf'ah and identify the evidence for each stage.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah arises upon sale, is confirmed by claiming, and is owned by taking possession.

Shuf'ah (pre-emption) is a right for a co-owner to take over a sold share. This right does not become automatically effective; it requires action from the pre-emptor. The classical Hanafi formulation divides the process into three distinct stages: obligation, establishment, and ownership. In this lesson, we will analyze each stage and the supporting proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three-stage model
Read the Arabic matn: 'والشفعة تجب بعقد البيع وتستقر بالإشهاد وتملك بالأخذ'. Note the three verbs: تجب (becomes obligatory), تستقر (becomes established), تملك (is owned). Each corresponds to a stage.
2
Understand the first stage: obligation upon sale
The right arises at the moment of the sale contract. The pre-emptor does not need to have knowledge yet. This is supported by Ibn Abi Layla's statement that no shuf'ah occurs until the sale occurs.
This is a haqq wujubi, not a religious duty.
3
Understand the second stage: establishment by ishhad
The right becomes firm only when the pre-emptor formally claims it by bearing witness. This prevents loss due to delay and is supported by the hadith 'Shuf'ah is like the untethering of a hobble' – which implies promptness.
Without ishhad, the right can be lost if the pre-emptor delays without excuse.
4
Understand the third stage: ownership by taking
Ownership transfers only when the pre-emptor physically takes possession, either by the buyer's surrender or a judge's ruling. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that transfer of ownership requires delivery in many cases.
At this point, the pre-emptor becomes the owner and the buyer must be compensated.
5
Review the proofs
The passage cites three proofs: (1) Ibn Abi Layla's statement, (2) the hadith of the hobble, (3) al-Sha'bi's statement. Each supports the need for the sale to occur first and the pre-emptor to act promptly.
These are ahad hadith and statements of tabi'in, considered valid proofs in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالشُّفْعَةُ تَجِبُ بِعَقْدِ الْبَيْعِ وَتَسْتَقِرُّ بِالْإِشْهَادِ وَتُمْلَكُ بِالْأَخْذِ إِذَا سَلَّمَهَا الْمُشْتَرِي، أَوْ حَكَمَ بِمَا حَاكِمٌ
وجه (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَالشُّفْعَةُ تَجِبُ بِعَقْدِ الْبَيْعِ وَتَسْتَقِرُّ بِالْإِشْهَادِ \ وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي لَيْلَى: «لا يَقَعُ لَهُ شُفْعَةٌ حَتَّى يَقَعَ الْبَيْعُ، فَإِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَ»،(مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ : الشَّفِيعُ يَأْذَنُ قَبْلَ الْبَيْعِ، وَكَمْ وَقْتُهَا، نمبر 14404)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالشُّفْعَةُ تَجِبُ بِعَقْدِ الْبَيْعِ وَتَسْتَقِرُّ بِالْإِشْهَادِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الشُّفْعَةُ كَحَلِّ الْعِقَالِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ طَلَبِ الشُّفْعَةِ، نمبر 2500/السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ رِوَايَةِ أَلْفَاظِ مُنْكَرَةٍ يَذْكُرُهَا بَعْضُ الْفُقَهَاءِ فِي مَسَائِل الشُّفْعَةِ، نمبر 11589)
وجه : (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَالشُّفْعَةُ تَجِبُ بِعَقْدِ الْبَيْعِ وَتَسْتَقِرُّ بِالْإِشْهَادِ \ وَقَالَ الشَّعْبِيُّ مَنْ بِيعَتْ شُفْعَتُهُ وَهُوَ شَاهِدٌ لَا يُغَيِّرُهَا فَلَا شُفْعَةَ لَهُ ، بخاري شريف بَابٌ: بَابُ عَرْضِ الشُّفْعَةِ عَلَى صَاحِبِهَا قَبْلَ الْبَيْعِ ، نمبر 2258/مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ : الشَّفِيعُ يَأْذَنُ قَبْلَ الْبَيْعِ، وَكَمْ وَقْتُهَا ، نمبر 14405)
And shuf'ah becomes obligatory with the contract of sale, becomes established by bearing witness, and is owned by taking when the buyer surrenders it, or a judge rules. Proof (1) The saying of the tabi'i for establishing that shuf'ah becomes obligatory with the contract of sale and becomes established by bearing witness: Ibn Abi Layla said: 'No shuf'ah occurs for him until the sale occurs; then if he wishes he takes, and if he wishes he leaves.' Proof (2) The hadith for establishing that shuf'ah becomes obligatory with the contract of sale and becomes established by bearing witness: From Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Shuf'ah is like the untethering of a camel's hobble.' (meaning it must be taken promptly). Proof (3) The saying of the tabi'i for establishing that shuf'ah becomes obligatory with the contract of sale and becomes established by bearing witness: Al-Sha'bi said: 'Whoever's shuf'ah is sold while he is present and does not change it (i.e., claim it), then there is no shuf'ah for him.'
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage describes the three stages of shuf'ah. First, shuf'ah becomes wajib (obligatory as a right) at the moment the sale contract is concluded. This means the pre-emptor's right comes into existence immediately, even if the sale is not yet known to him. Second, this right becomes established or confirmed (tastaqirru) by the pre-emptor bearing witness (ishhad) that he is claiming his right. This prevents the right from being lost due to delay. Third, the pre-emptor actually owns the property (tumlaku) by taking possession (al-akhdh) when the buyer voluntarily surrenders the property to him or a judge rules in his favor. The proofs include: (1) Ibn Abi Layla's statement that no shuf'ah occurs until the sale, then he may take or leave – indicating the right arises from the contract. (2) The hadith 'Shuf'ah is like the untethering of a camel's hobble' – meaning it must be taken promptly, without delay. (3) Al-Sha'bi's statement that if a person's shuf'ah is sold while he is present and he does not object, he loses his right – showing the need for prompt action. In Hanafi fiqh, the ishhad is a requirement to establish the right; if the pre-emptor delays without valid excuse, the right is lost.

Key Terms
شُفْعَة (shuf'ah): The right to take over the share sold to a new buyer, at the same price and terms.
إِشْهَاد (ishhād): The act of the pre-emptor formally bearing witness (calling witnesses) to his claim, thereby establishing his right.
تَمْلِيك بِالْأَخْذ (tamlīk bi al-akhdh): Ownership of the property is transferred to the pre-emptor by physically taking possession after the buyer surrenders or a judge rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
At what point does shuf'ah become wajib (obligatory as a right)?
A) Upon the pre-emptor bearing witness
B) Upon the buyer taking possession
C) Upon the contract of sale
D) Upon the judge's ruling

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is not automatic; it requires timely claiming by bearing witness to be established.

Procedure and Promptness for Claiming Shuf'ah
Explains procedural steps and time limit for claiming shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two-stage procedural steps for claiming shuf'ah and explain the Hanafi ruling on promptness including the intra-madhhab difference regarding the month limit.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is a right that must be seized immediately — delay after knowledge invalidates it.

This lesson details the precise steps a pre-emptor must take upon learning of a sale. You will learn the obligation to bear witness in the same gathering, the requirement to then formally notify the seller or buyer, and the critical importance of acting without delay. The passage also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over a fixed time limit after the initial claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the pre-emptor required to do upon learning of the sale? The text states he must 'bear witness in that same gathering to his claim' and then 'rise and bear witness against the seller, buyer, or at the property.' The ruling is that this claim must be made immediately; delay invalidates the right.
The initial ishhad (bearing witness to the claim) is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: (1) the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'Shuf'ah is like the untethering of a hobble,' and (2) the saying of Shurayh: 'Shuf'ah is only for the one who hastens.'
Both proofs emphasize speed and promptness.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith compares shuf'ah to the immediate release of a hobbled animal — if not caught quickly, it escapes. This indicates that the right must be seized without hesitation. Shurayh's statement uses 'wāthabahā' (hastened), directly requiring prompt action.
The imperative to hasten shows that delay is contrary to the nature of shuf'ah.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad adds that if the pre-emptor delays for a month after the initial ishhad, the right becomes invalid. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf do not fix a specific period; they consider delay with excuse acceptable.
The dispute is over whether a fixed time limit exists.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that the pre-emptor must act promptly; undue delay without excuse invalidates the right. The month is a guideline, not a strict limit. The majority including Abu Hanifa do not require a month deadline.
In practice, the pre-emptor should act as soon as he learns of the sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا عَلِمَ الشَّفِيعُ بِالْبَيْعِ أَشْهَدَ فِي مَجْلِسِهِ ذَلِكَ عَلَى الْمُطَالَبَةِ ثُمَّ يَنْهَضُ مِنْهُ فَيُشْهِدُ عَلَى الْبَائِعِ إِنْ كَانَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ أَوْ عَلَى الْمُبْتَاعِ، أَوْ عِنْدَ الْعَقَارِ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ إِنْ تَرَكَهَا شَهْرًا بَعْدَ الْإِشْهَادِ بَطَلَتْ
توجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا عَلِمَ الشَّفِيعُ بِالْبَيْعِ أَشْهَدَ فِي مَجْلِسِهِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الشُّفْعَةُ كَحَ الْعِقَالِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ طَلَبِ الشُّفْعَةِ، نمبر 2500/السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ رِوَايَةِ أَلْفَاظِ مُنْكَرَةِ يَذْكُرُهَا بَعْضُ الْفُقَهَاءِ فِي مَسَائِلِ الشُّفْعَةِ، 11589) وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا عَلِمَ الشَّفِيعُ بِالْبَيْعِ أَشْهَدَ فِي مَجْلِسِهِ \ عَنِ الحَسَنِ بْن عُمَارَةَ، عَنْ رَجُلٍ، عَنْ شُرَيْحٍ قَالَ: «إِنَّمَا الشُّفْعَةُ لِمَنْ وَاثَبَهَا»،( مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ: الشَّفِيعُ يَأْذَنُ قَبْلَ الْبَيْعِ، وَكَمْ وَقْتُهَا ،غبر 14406)
And when the pre-emptor learns of the sale, he should bear witness in that same gathering to his claim. Then he rises from it and bears witness against the seller if the sold property is in his possession, or against the buyer, or at the property. And Muhammad said: If he leaves it for a month after bearing witness, it becomes invalid. Proof (1) The hadith for establishing that when the pre-emptor learns of the sale, he should bear witness in his gathering: From Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Shuf'ah is like the untethering of a hobble.' Proof (2) The saying of the tabi'i for establishing that when the pre-emptor learns of the sale, he should bear witness in his gathering: From al-Hasan ibn 'Umarah, from a man, from Shurayh, he said: 'Shuf'ah is only for the one who hastens to it.'
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage details the procedure for the pre-emptor. Upon learning of the sale, he must immediately (in that same gathering) bear witness that he is claiming his right. This is the first step: ishhad upon knowledge. Then he must take action by going to the seller, the buyer, or the property to formally assert his claim. This is the second step: ishhad against the party. Imam Muhammad adds that if the pre-emptor delays for a month after the initial ishhad without pursuing the claim, his right becomes invalid. The proofs rest on the hadith comparing shuf'ah to an untethered hobble, indicating speed is required, and Shurayh's statement that shuf'ah is only for one who hastens. In Hanafi fiqh, the pre-emptor must act without unnecessary delay; the month limit is a guideline. The relied-upon position is that the pre-emptor should claim as soon as he knows, and if he delays without excuse, he forfeits his right.

Key Terms
مَجْلِس (majlis): The gathering in which the pre-emptor learns of the sale. He must bear witness in that same gathering without delay.
إِشْهَاد عَلَى الْمُطَالَبَة (ishhād 'alā al-muṭālabah): Bearing witness (calling witnesses) to the fact that the pre-emptor is claiming his right of shuf'ah.
وَاثَبَهَا (wāthabahā): Hastened to it; from the saying of Shurayh that shuf'ah is only for the one who hastens to claim it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Imam Muhammad say about a one-month delay after bearing witness?
A) The right becomes stronger
B) The right is invalidated
C) The pre-emptor must bear witness again
D) The sale becomes void

Key Takeaway
The right of shuf'ah is lost if the pre-emptor does not act immediately upon knowledge; delay without excuse invalidates the claim.

Shuf'ah Applies to Real Estate Even if Indivisible
Affirms shuf'ah for real estate with three hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that shuf'ah is wajib in real estate even if the property is indivisible, and cite the three primary hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is a confirmed right in real estate, whether divisible or not, based on prophetic hadith.

This lesson establishes the scope of shuf'ah (pre-emption) in Hanafi fiqh. The key point: shuf'ah applies only to immovable property ('aqar), and it applies even if the property cannot be physically divided. Three hadith provide the foundation for this ruling. Understanding this clarifies when the right of pre-emption exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the main statement: shuf'ah is obligatory (wajib) in real estate.
The term 'wajib' here means a confirmed legal right, not a religious obligation.
2
Identify the condition
Note the phrase 'even if it is something that cannot be divided' (wa in kana mimma la yuqsam).
This emphasizes that indivisibility does not negate the right.
3
Analyze the first hadith
The hadith of Jabir: a co-owner in a residence or palm tree must inform his partner before selling; the partner has the right to take it.
This establishes shuf'ah for undivided shares in real estate.
4
Analyze the second hadith
The hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'No shuf'ah except in a house or real estate.'
The negation with exception restricts shuf'ah exclusively to real estate.
5
Analyze the third hadith
The hadith of Jabir: the Prophet ruled with shuf'ah in everything not yet divided; once boundaries are fixed, no shuf'ah.
This confirms shuf'ah applies to undivided shares and ends upon partition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالشُّفْعَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ فِي الْعَقَارِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا لَا يُقْسَمُ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالشُّفْعَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ فِي الْعَقَارِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا لَا يُقْسَمُ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ. قَالَ : قَالَ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ شَرِيكَ فِي رَبْعَةٍ أَوْ نَخْلِ، فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَبِيعَ حَتَّى يُؤْذِنَ شَرِيكَهُ. فَإِنْ رَضِيَ أَخَذَ وَإِنْ كَرِهَ تَرَكَ)، (مسلم شريف : باب الشفعة،نمبر1608/سنن ابوداود شريف، باب في الشُّفْعَةِ، نمبر 3513)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالشُّفْعَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ فِي الْعَقَارِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا لَا يُقْسَمُ اعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " لَا شُفْعَةَ إِلَّا فِي دَارٍ أَوْ عَقَارٍ " السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ لَا شُفْعَةَ فِيمَا يُنْقَلُ وَيُحَوِّلُ، غبر 11597)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَالشُّفْعَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ فِي الْعَقَارِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا لَا يُقْسَمُ أَعَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ الله رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «قَضَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالشُّفْعَةِ فِي كُلّ مَا لَمْ يُقْسَمْ، فَإِذَا وَقَعَتِ اخْدُودُ وَصُرِفَتِ الطُّرُقُ، فَلَا شُفْعَةَ»، ((بخاري شريف، كِتَابُ الشُّفْعَةِ، بَابٌ: الشُّفْعَةُ مَا لَمْ يُقْسَمْ فَإِذَا وَقَعَتِ الْخُدُودُ فَلَا شُفْعَةَ، نمبر 2257/ سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الشُّفْعَةِ، نمبر 3514/سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الرُّجُوعِ في الهبة، نمبر 1370
And shuf'ah is obligatory in real estate, even if it is something that cannot be divided. Proof (1) The hadith for establishing that shuf'ah is obligatory in real estate, even if it is something that cannot be divided: From Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever has a share in a residence or a palm tree, he should not sell until he informs his partner. Then if he is pleased, he takes; if he dislikes, he leaves.' Proof (2) The hadith for establishing that shuf'ah is obligatory in real estate, even if it is something that cannot be divided: From Abu Hurairah, he said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'No shuf'ah except in a house or real estate.' Proof (3) The hadith for establishing that shuf'ah is obligatory in real estate, even if it is something that cannot be divided: From Jabir ibn Abdillah (may Allah be pleased with them both), he said: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ ruled with shuf'ah in everything that had not been divided. But when boundaries are fixed and roads are allotted, there is no shuf'ah.'
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage establishes that shuf'ah is only applicable to real estate ('aqar), such as land, houses, and palm trees. It does not apply to movable property (manqulat). Furthermore, shuf'ah applies whether the property can be physically divided (yuqsam) or not. This means even if the property is too small to partition, the right of shuf'ah still exists. The proofs include: (1) The hadith of Jabir that a partner in a residence or palm tree cannot sell without informing his partner; if the partner wishes, he takes it. This shows shuf'ah in undivided shares. (2) The hadith of Abu Hurairah that there is no shuf'ah except in a house or real estate, limiting it to real property. (3) The hadith of Jabir that the Prophet ruled with shuf'ah in everything not yet divided, but once boundaries are fixed and roads separated (i.e., the property is partitioned), there is no shuf'ah. This aligns with the Hanafi view that shuf'ah applies to undivided shares in real estate.

Key Terms
عَقَار ('aqār): Real estate; immovable property such as land, houses, gardens, etc.
لَا يُقْسَم (lā yuqsam): That which cannot be divided physically or legally due to its small size or other reasons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, on what type of property is shuf'ah applicable?
A) Both movable and immovable property
B) Only immovable property (real estate)
C) Only divisible property
D) Only undivided property

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is a confirmed right in real estate, applying even to indivisible properties, based on explicit hadith.

Agency in Litigation: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on agency in litigation with disagreement among Hanafi imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on agency in litigation, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and identify the mufta bihi position along with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Agency in litigation is valid without the opponent's consent according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

When you need to go to court, you might appoint a lawyer. But does the other party have to agree? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this point. In this lesson, we examine the ruling of agency in litigation (al-tawkil bi al-khusumah) and the proofs used by the two sides, concluding with the operative view for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the contested matter: is the opponent's consent required for valid agency in litigation?
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
State that Abu Hanifa requires consent except when the principal is ill or traveling three days or more.
His basis: potential harm to the opponent.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
State that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow agency without consent unconditionally.
Their basis: general permissibility and public ease.
4
Examine the proofs
Analyze the hadith on averting punishments and the practice of Ali (ra) as evidence for the permissive view.
The hadith supports leniency, which aligns with removing obstacles in litigation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its thamarah
State that later Hanafi authorities prefer the Sahibayn's view. The practical effect: one can appoint a lawyer without the opponent's consent in all cases.
This is the operative position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْوَكَالَةِ وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ لَا يَجُوزُ التَّوْكِيلُ بِالْخُصُومَةِ إِلَّا بِرِضًا الْخَصْمِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُوَكَّلُ مَرِيضًا أَوْ غَائِبًا مَسِيرَةَ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فَصَاعِدًا وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَجُوزُ التَّوْكِيلُ بِغَيْرِ رِضَا الْخَصْمِ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «ادْرَءُوا الحدُودَ عَن المُسْلِمِينَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُمْ، فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُ مَخْرَجْ فَخَلُّوا سَبِيلَهُ، فَإِنَّ الإِمَامَ أَنْ يُخْطِئَ فِي العَفْوِ خَيْرٌ مِنْ أَنْ يُخْطِئَ فِي العُقُوبَةِ» عَنْ عَبْدِ اللهِ بْنِ جَعْفَرٍ قَالَ: "كَانَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبي طَالِب يَكْرَهُ الْخُصُومَةَ، فَكَانَ إِذَا كَانَتْ لَهُ خُصُومَةٌ وَكَلَ فِيهَا عَقِيلَ بْنَ أَبِي طَالِبٍ، فَلَمَّا كَبِرَ عَقِيلٌ وَكَلَنِي"
Book of Agency. Abu Hanifa said: Agency in litigation is not permissible except with the consent of the opponent, unless the principal is ill or absent for a distance of three days or more. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Agency is permissible without the consent of the opponent. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Avert the prescribed punishments from the Muslims as much as you can; if there is a way out, let him go, for the imam to err in pardoning is better than to err in punishing.' From Abdullah ibn Ja'far: 'Ali ibn Abi Talib disliked litigation, so when he had a case, he appointed Aqeel ibn Abi Talib as his agent; when Aqeel grew old, he appointed me.'
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding agency in litigation (al-tawkil bi al-khusumah). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such agency is only valid with the consent of the opposing party, except when the principal is ill or traveling a distance of three days or more, in which case the opponent's consent is not required. His students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, allow agency in litigation without the opponent's consent unconditionally. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, as it is more practical and avoids hardship. The text then provides proofs: a hadith encouraging leniency in punishments supports the permissive view, and the practice of Ali (ra) appointing agents in litigation is cited as corroboration.

Key Terms
التوكيل بالخصومة (al-tawkil bi al-khusumah): Appointing an agent to represent the principal in court litigation.
الخصم (al-khasm): The opposing party in litigation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when is agency in litigation valid?
A) Only with the opponent's consent
B) Only if the principal is ill or traveling
C) Generally, without requiring the opponent's consent
D) Only if the agent is a relative

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi allows appointing a lawyer without the opponent's consent in all cases.
