Hibah of Undivided Divisible Property Requires Possession and Division
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on gift validity condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires possession and division for a valid gift of divisible property, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A gift of undivided property is invalid because possession of an undivided share is legally impossible.

This lesson delves into a key condition for the validity of hibah (gift) in Hanafi fiqh: the gifted property must be possessed and divided if it is divisible. The Hanafi school holds that without physical separation and delivery, the gift is void. This position is contested by the Shafi'i school, which validates gifts of undivided shares based on prophetic practice. We will examine the proofs from both sides and understand the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and define the property type
Start with the precise Hanafi ruling: a gift of divisible property (mā yuqsam) is not valid unless the property is physically taken possession of and divided. Understand the term 'mā yuqsam' (divisible property) as distinct from indivisible property.
Divisible property includes land, buildings, animals – anything that can be split without significant harm.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proofs from the Tabi'i and hadith
Examine the three proofs cited: the letter of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz requiring separation, the statement of Ibn Shubrumah, and the hadith of Abu Qatadah where the Prophet accepted a specific haunch. Determine how each proof supports the requirement of division and possession.
The hadith shows the Prophet accepting a divided piece, implying that the gift of the whole animal was not valid until it was divided.
3
Present the Shafi'i objection and their proofs
Identify the two Shafi'i proofs: the Prophet gifting the entire booty of Hawazin while undivided, and the hadith of the boy who shared his drink without division. Understand why these suggest that undivided property can be gifted.
These actions seem to contradict the Hanafi requirement.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proofs
The Hanafi school distinguishes the cases: the Hawazin gift may be a special transaction (e.g., a peace settlement or a grant from booty), and the drink hadith involves a specific share already identified (the boy's own cup). The principle remains that possession of an undivided share is legally impossible.
The response relies on the maxim that what cannot be possessed individually cannot be validly gifted.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Apply the dispute to a real scenario: a person gives an undivided half of a house as a gift. Under Hanafi, the gift is invalid until the house is divided and the share delivered. Under Shafi'i, the gift is valid immediately.
The ruling affects everyday transactions, such as gifting a share in a jointly owned property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا تَجُوزُ الْهِبَةُ فِيمَا يُقْسَمُ إِلَّا مَحُوزَةً مَقْسُومَةً
وَجْهُ (1) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا تَجُوزُ الْهِبَةُ فِيمَا يُقْسَمُ إِلَّا مَحُوزَةً مَقْسُومَةً قَالَ كَتَبَ عُمَرُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ أَنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ مِنَ النُّحْلِ إِلَّا مَا عُزِلَ وَأُفْرِدَ وَأُعْلِمَ. (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ النُّحْلِ، رقم 16514)
وَجْهُ (2) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا تَجُوزُ الْهِبَةُ فِيمَا يُقْسَمُ إِلَّا مَحُوزَةً مَقْسُومَةً عَنِ ابْنِ شُبْرُمَةَ قَالَ إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مَا وَهَبَ لَهُ صَاحِبُهُ فَلَيْسَ بِشَيْءٍ. (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ حِيَازَةِ مَا وَهَبَ أَحَدُهُمَا لِصَاحِبِهِ، رقم 16570)
وَجْهُ (3) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا تَجُوزُ الْهِبَةُ فِيمَا يُقْسَمُ إِلَّا مَحُوزَةً مَقْسُومَةً عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ السَّلَمِيِّ عَنْ أَبِيهِ فَشَدَدْتُ عَلَى الْحِمَارِ فَعَقَرْتُهُ ثُمَّ جِئْتُ بِهِ وَقَدْ مَاتَ فَوَقَعُوا فِيهِ يَأْكُلُونَهُ ثُمَّ إِنَّهُمْ شَكُوا فِي أَكْلِهِمْ إِيَّاهُ وَهُمْ حُرُمٌ فَرُحْنَا وَخَبَأْتُ الْعَصْدَ مَعِي فَأَدْرَكْنَا رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَسَأَلْنَاهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ فَقَالَ مَعَكُمْ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ فَقُلْتُ نَعَمْ فَنَاوَلْتُهُ الْعَصْدَ فَأَكَلَهَا حَتَّى نَفِدَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ. (بخاري، بَابُ مَنِ اسْتَوْهَبَ مِنْ أَصْحَابِهِ شَيْئًا، رقم 2570)
وَجْهُ (1) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا تَجُوزُ الْهِبَةُ فِيمَا يُقْسَمُ إِلَّا مَحُوزَةً مَقْسُومَةً وَقَدْ وَهَبَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَصْحَابُهُ لِهَوَازِنَ مَا غَنِمُوا مِنْهُمْ وَهُوَ غَيْرُ مَقْسُومٍ. (بخاري، بَابُ الْهِبَةِ الْمَقْبُوضَةِ وَغَيْرِ الْمَقْبُوضَةِ وَالْمَقْسُومَةِ وَغَيْرِ الْمَقْسُومَةِ، رقم 2603)
وَجْهُ (2) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا تَجُوزُ الْهِبَةُ فِيمَا يُقْسَمُ إِلَّا مَحُوزَةً مَقْسُومَةً عَنْ سَهْلِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أُتِيَ بِشَرَابٍ وَعَنْ يَمِينِهِ غُلَامٌ وَعَنْ يَسَارِهِ أَشْيَاخٌ فَقَالَ لِلْغُلَامِ أَتَأْذَنُ لِي أَنْ أُعْطِيَ هَؤُلَاءِ فَقَالَ الْغُلَامُ لَا وَاللَّهِ لَا أُوثِرُ بِنَصِيبِي مِنْكَ أَحَدًا فَتَلَّهُ فِي يَدِهِ. (بخاري، بَابُ الْهِبَةِ الْمَقْبُوضَةِ وَغَيْرِ الْمَقْبُوضَةِ، رقم 2605)
اصول: ہبہ میں کلی طور پر موہوب پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے، اس لئے تقسیم شدہ ہو تا کہ قبضہ ہو سکے۔
And gift is not valid in what is divisible except as possessed (and) divided. Proof 1: The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing that gift is not valid in what is divisible except as possessed and divided: He said: Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz wrote that no gift (nuhl) is valid except what is set aside, separated, and made known. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on Nuhl, no. 16514). Proof 2: The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing that gift is not valid in what is divisible except as possessed and divided: from Ibn Shubrumah, he said: If each of them does not have what he gifted to his companion, then it is nothing. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on Possession of What One Gifts to Another, no. 16570). Proof 3: The hadith for establishing that gift is not valid in what is divisible except as possessed and divided: from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatadah al-Salami from his father: I pressed the donkey and hamstrung it, then I came with it and it had died, so they fell upon it eating it. Then they doubted about their eating it while they were in ihram. So we left and I hid the haunch with me, then we caught up with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and asked him about that. He said: 'Do you have any of it with you?' I said: 'Yes.' So I handed him the haunch and he ate it until he finished it while he was in ihram. (Bukhari, Chapter on Whoever Asks for a Gift from His Companions, no. 2570). Proof 1: The proof of al-Shafi'i for establishing that gift is not valid in what is divisible except as possessed and divided: The Prophet (peace be upon him) and his Companions gifted to Hawazin what they had taken as booty from them while it was undivided. (Bukhari, Chapter on Gift Taken Possession and Not Taken Possession, and Divided and Undivided, no. 2603). Proof 2: The proof of al-Shafi'i for establishing that gift is not valid in what is divisible except as possessed and divided: from Sahl ibn Sa'd that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was brought a drink, and on his right side was a boy, and on his left side were elders. He said to the boy: 'Will you permit me to give these (elders)?' The boy said: 'No, by Allah, I will not give precedence to anyone over my share from you.' So he placed it in his hand. (Bukhari, Chapter on Gift Taken Possession and Not Taken Possession, no. 2605). Principle: In gift, possession of the gifted item is necessary in totality; therefore it must be divided so that possession can be effectuated.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that a gift of undivided property (mā lā yuqsam) is not valid unless it is physically separated and delivered. The author provides proofs from the sayings of the Tabi'in (Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and Ibn Shubrumah) and a hadith from Abu Qatadah about the Prophet accepting a piece of game while in ihram, which indicates that the gift was of a specific, divided portion. Then the author addresses the Shafi'i objection: Shafi'i argues that the Prophet gifted the entire booty of Hawazin while undivided, and that he gave a drink to a boy without dividing it. The Hanafi response, implied in the usul note, is that possession is necessary; undivided property cannot be validly gifted because possession of an undivided share is legally impossible. Therefore, the property must be divided first. This is a clear inter-madhhab dispute.

Key Terms
محوزة مقسومة (mahūzatan maqsūmatan): Possessed and divided; means the gifted property must be physically taken possession of and separated from any shared ownership.
ما يقسم (mā yuqsam): Divisible property; property that can be divided into shares without loss of utility, e.g., land, buildings, animals. Opposite of 'mā lā yuqsam' (indivisible).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented, why is a gift of an undivided share of a house (which is divisible) considered invalid?
A) Because the donor did not utter the correct formula.
B) Because possession of an undivided share is legally impossible.
C) Because gifts of real estate require court approval.
D) Because the donee must be present at the time of gift.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires that gifts of divisible property be physically divided and delivered; without this, the gift is invalid (fasid), unlike the Shafi'i school which allows gifts of undivided shares.

Validity of Gift in Divisible Property: Possession After Division Required
Commentary on Quduri's matn for hibah with hadith proofs and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a gift of divisible property, cite the hadith proofs, and explain why the Hanafi school rejects the Shafi'i argument from the Hawazin booty and drink hadith.

Core Idea
A gift of divisible property is invalid without possession after division – the contract alone does not transfer ownership.

In this lesson, we unpack a fundamental condition for gift (hibah) in Hanafi fiqh: the requirement of physical possession (qabd) after the property has been divided. The source text from al-Quduri states this rule succinctly, and the accompanying commentary provides hadith-based proofs. We also examine the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response, which clarifies why the rule is not contradicted by certain prophetic practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a gift of divisible property (e.g., land, goods). Ruling: not valid (لا تجوز) unless it is possessed after division (محوزة مقسومة).
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The hadith of Umar (Bukhari) about not taking back a charity indicates that possession changes ownership. The practice of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz requiring separation and marking. Ibn Shubruma's statement that if each does not have what was gifted, it is nothing.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's prohibition of taking back a charity implies the gift was already effective through possession. Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz's condition of isolation shows that mere contractual words are insufficient.
4
Identify the opposing school and its proof
The Shafi'i school argues that a gift of undivided property is valid, citing the Prophet gifting Hawazin booty while still undivided and the hadith of the drink given to a boy instead of elders.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that those cases involved indivisible property (booty considered a single entity) or specific concessions. The general rule requires division and possession for divisible property. The tarjih (preferred view) is the Hanafi position, which is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْهِبَةِ. وَلَا تَجُوزُ الْهِبَةُ فِيمَا يُقْسَمُ إِلَّا مَحُوزَةً مَقْسُومَةً. وَتَنْعَقِدُ الْهِبَةُ بِقَوْلِهِ وَهَبْتُكَ وَنَحَلْتُكَ. عَنْ عُمَرَ: «حَمَلْتُ عَلَى فَرَسٍ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ، فَرَأَيْتُهُ يُبَاعُ، فَسَأَلْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: لَا تَشْتَرِ وَلَا تَعُدْ فِي صَدَقَتِكَ.» (بخاري 2636). عَنْ عُمَرَ بْنِ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ: «أَنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ مِنَ النُّحْلِ إِلَّا مَا عُزِلَ وَأُفْرِدَ وَأُعْلِمَ.» (مصنف عبد الرزاق 16514). عَنِ ابْنِ شُبْرُمَةَ: «إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مَا وَهَبَ لَهُ صَاحِبُهُ فَلَيْسَ بِشَيْءٍ.» (مصنف عبد الرزاق 16570). عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ: فَشَدَدْتُ عَلَى الْحِمَارِ فَعَقَرْتُهُ، ثُمَّ جِئْتُ بِهِ وَقَدْ مَاتَ، فَوَقَعُوا فِيهِ يَأْكُلُونَهُ، ثُمَّ إِنَّهُمْ شَكُوا فِي أَكْلِهِمْ إِيَّاهُ وَهُمْ حُرُمٌ، فَرُحْنَا وَخَبَأْتُ الْعَضْدَ مَعِي، فَأَدْرَكْنَا رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَسَأَلْنَاهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، فَقَالَ: مَعَكُمْ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ، فَقُلْتُ: نَعَمْ، فَنَاوَلْتُهُ الْعَضْدَ فَأَكَلَهَا حَتَّى نَفِدَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ. (بخاري 2570). وَدَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ: الْحَدِيثُ فِي هِبَةِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَصْحَابِهِ لِهَوَازِنَ مَا غَنِمُوا مِنْهُمْ وَهُوَ غَيْرُ مَقْسُومٍ. (بخاري 2603). وَالْحَدِيثُ عَنْ سَهْلِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ أُتِيَ بِشَرَابٍ، وَعَنْ يَمِينِهِ غُلَامٌ، وَعَنْ يَسَارِهِ أَشْيَاخٌ، فَقَالَ لِلْغُلَامِ: أَتَأْذَنُ لِي أَنْ أُعْطِيَ هَؤُلَاءِ، فَقَالَ الْغُلَامُ: لَا، فَتَلَّهُ فِي يَدِهِ. (بخاري 2605). وَهِبَةُ الْمُشَاعِ فِي مَا لَا يُقْسَمُ جَائِزَةٌ. وَمَنْ وُهِبَ شِقْصًا مُشَاعًا فَالْهِبَةُ فَاسِدَةٌ فَإِنْ قَسَّمَهُ وَسَلَّمَهُ جَازَ. وَلَوْ وَهَبَ دَقِيقًا فِي حِنْطَةٍ أَوْ دُهْنًا فِي سِمْسِمٍ فَالْهِبَةُ فَاسِدَةٌ فَإِنْ طَحَنَ وَسَلَّمَ لَمْ يَجُزْ. وَإِنْ كَانَتْ الْعَيْنُ الْمَوْهُوبَةُ فِي يَدِ الْمَوْهُوبِ لَهُ مَلَكَهَا بِالْهِبَةِ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يُجَدِّدْ فِيهَا قَبْضًا. وَإِذَا وَهَبَ الْأَبُ لِابْنِهِ الصَّغِيرِ هِبَةً مَلَكَهَا الْإِبْنُ بِالْعَقْدِ فَإِنْ وَهَبَ لَهُ أَجْنَبِيٌّ هِبَةً تَمَّتْ بِقَبْضِ الْأَبِ. وَإِذَا وُهِبَ لِلْيَتِيمِ هِبَةٌ فَقَبَضَهَا لَهُ وَلِيُّهُ جَازَ. عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ: (الْحَدِيثُ السَّابِقُ). عَنِ ابْنِ شُبْرُمَةَ: سَأَلْتُهُ عَنْ شِقْصٍ مُشَاعٍ فَقَالَ: «إِذَا سَمَّى فَجَعَلَ لَهُ مِائَةَ دِينَارٍ مِنْ مَالِهِ فَهُوَ جَائِزٌ، وَإِنْ سَمَّى ثُلُثًا أَوْ رُبُعًا لَمْ يَجُزْ حَتَّى يُقَسَّمَ.» (مصنف عبد الرزاق 16531). عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ: كُنَّا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ في سَفَرٍ وَكُنْتُ عَلَى بَكْرٍ صَعْبٍ فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ لِعُمَرَ: بِعْنِيهِ فَابْتَاعَهُ فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ: هُوَ لَكَ يَا عَبْدَ اللهِ. (بخاري 2611). عَنْ عُثْمَانَ بْنِ عَفَّانَ: «مَنْ نَحَلَ وَلَدًا لَهُ صَغِيرًا لَمْ يَبْلُغْ أَنْ يَكُونَ تَحْلَهُ، فَأَعْلَنَ بِهَا وَأَشْهَدَ عَلَيْهَا، فَهِيَ جَائِزَةٌ وَإِنْ وَلِيَهَا أَبُوهُ.» (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي 11952). عَنْ أَبِي مُوسَى الْأَشْعَرِيِّ قَالَ: قَالَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ: «الْأَنْحَالُ مِيرَاثٌ مَا لَمْ يُقْبَضْ.»
Book of Gifts. And the gift is not valid in what is divisible except taken possession of after division. And the gift is concluded by his saying 'I gifted you' and 'I bestowed upon you'. From Umar: 'I mounted a horse in the path of Allah, then I saw it being sold, so I asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he said: Do not buy it and do not take back your charity.' (Bukhari 2636). From Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz: 'No gift is valid except what is separated, isolated, and made known.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq 16514). From Ibn Shubruma: 'If each of them does not have what his companion gifted him, then it is nothing.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq 16570). From Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father: '...I pressed the donkey and wounded it, then I brought it dead, they fell upon it eating, then they doubted while in ihram, ... so we went and I hid the arm, then we caught the Prophet and asked, he said: Do you have any of it? I said yes, so I gave him the arm and he ate it until it was finished while he was in ihram.' (Bukhari 2570). And the proof of al-Shafi'i: The hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions gifting to Hawazin what they had taken as booty from them while it was undivided. (Bukhari 2603). And the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd: 'The Prophet was brought a drink, on his right a boy, on his left elders, he said to the boy: Do you permit me to give these? The boy said no, so he placed it in his hand.' (Bukhari 2605). And the gift of common ownership in what is not divisible is valid. And whoever is gifted an undivided share, the gift is invalid, but if he divides it and hands it over, it becomes valid. And if he gifted flour in wheat or oil in sesame, the gift is invalid; if he grinds and hands over, it is not valid. And if the gifted property is already in the hand of the donee, he owns it by the gift, even if he does not renew possession. And when the father gifts to his minor child, the child owns it by the contract; if a stranger gifts to him, it is completed by the father's possession. And if a gift is given to an orphan, and his guardian takes possession for him, it is valid. From Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada: (the previous hadith). From Ibn Shubruma: I asked him about an undivided share, and he said: 'If he specifies and makes for him a hundred dinars from his wealth, it is valid; if he specifies a third or a fourth, it is not valid until it is divided.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq 16531). From Ibn Umar: 'We were with the Prophet on a journey, I was on a difficult camel, the Prophet said to Umar: Sell it to me, so he bought it, then the Prophet said: It is for you, O Abdullah.' (Bukhari 2611). From Uthman ibn Affan: 'Whoever gives a gift to his minor child who has not reached the age of disposal, and he publicizes it and witnesses it, it is valid even if his father takes possession of it.' (Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi 11952). From Abu Musa al-Ashari said: Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'Gifts are inheritance as long as they are not taken possession of.'
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of al-Quduri regarding the conditions for validity of gifts (hibah). It states rulings and provides proofs from hadith, along with a response to the Shafi'i position. The author first presents the ruling that a gift of divisible property is not valid unless it is taken possession of after division (محوزة مقسومة). This means that if the property is divisible (like land or goods that can be split), mere contract is insufficient; the donor must physically hand over the specific part to the donee. This is supported by several evidences: the hadith of Umar about not taking back charity, the practice of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, and the statement of Ibn Shubruma. Then the author addresses the Shafi'i proof that the Prophet gifted booty to Hawazin while still undivided. The Hanafi response (implied) is that such a gift was a specific exception or that the property was indivisible at the time. The second Shafi'i hadith about the drink is also addressed; the Hanafis likely interpret it as a case of indivisible property (a single drink). The passage then continues with rulings on gift of common ownership (مشاع) in indivisible property: it is valid. But if someone is gifted a share in divisible property, the gift is invalid unless divided and possession given. Similarly, if flour is gifted in wheat (not yet ground) or oil in sesame, the gift is invalid; even if ground and delivered, it doesn't become valid because the subject matter was not specified at the time of contract. However, if the gifted property is already in the donee's possession (e.g., he was holding it as a deposit), the gift is complete without new possession. For gifts to minors: a father's gift to his minor child is valid by contract alone because the father acts as guardian. If a stranger gifts to a minor, it requires the father's possession. For an orphan, the guardian's possession suffices. The proofs include hadith from Ibn Umar, the practice of Uthman, and the statement of Umar.

Key Terms
هِبَة (hibah): A contract that transfers ownership of a specific property without compensation.
قَبْض (qabd): Physical possession or taking delivery of the gifted property.
مُشَاع (mushā'): Undivided share in a property held in common.
شِقْص (shiqs): A share or portion, often used for a share in an undivided property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a gift of a divisible property is valid only if:
A) The donor utters the words 'I gift you' and the donee accepts.
B) The donee takes physical possession after the property has been divided.
C) The property is worth at least 10 dirhams.
D) The gift is witnessed by two male witnesses.

Key Takeaway
A gift of divisible property requires possession after division; without it, the contract alone does not transfer ownership.

Subsidiary Rulings on Gift: Undivided Shares, Mixed Goods, and Gifts to Minors
Rulings on gift of undivided shares, mixed goods, and minors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid gifts of undivided shares based on divisibility, and apply the rules for gifts of mixed goods and gifts to minors.

Core Idea
A gift of an undivided share is valid only in indivisible property; in divisible property it requires division. Gifts to minors are valid with guardian's possession.

Having established the core condition for divisible property, the text now addresses several subsidiary issues: the gift of an undivided share (mushā') in different types of property, the peculiar case of gifting flour in wheat or oil in sesame, and the rules for gifts to minors and orphans. These nuanced rulings demonstrate how the principle of possession after division applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property type
Determine if the gifted property is divisible or indivisible. The ruling depends on this distinction.
2
Apply the rule for undivided share
If property is indivisible, the gift of an undivided share is valid. If divisible, the gift is invalid until division and possession.
3
Handle mixed goods
If the gift is of flour in wheat or oil in sesame, the gift is invalid because the subject matter is not specifically identified. Even if processed later, it does not become valid.
4
Check possession already in donee's hand
If the gifted item is already in the donee's possession, ownership transfers by contract alone; no new possession needed.
5
Apply rules for gifts to minors
Father's gift to his minor child is valid by contract alone. Stranger's gift to minor requires father's possession. Orphan's gift requires guardian's possession.

Source Text

كِتَابُ الْهِبَةِ. وَلَا تَجُوزُ الْهِبَةُ فِيمَا يُقْسَمُ إِلَّا مَحُوزَةً مَقْسُومَةً. وَتَنْعَقِدُ الْهِبَةُ بِقَوْلِهِ وَهَبْتُكَ وَنَحَلْتُكَ. عَنْ عُمَرَ: «حَمَلْتُ عَلَى فَرَسٍ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ، فَرَأَيْتُهُ يُبَاعُ، فَسَأَلْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: لَا تَشْتَرِ وَلَا تَعُدْ فِي صَدَقَتِكَ.» (بخاري 2636). عَنْ عُمَرَ بْنِ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ: «أَنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ مِنَ النُّحْلِ إِلَّا مَا عُزِلَ وَأُفْرِدَ وَأُعْلِمَ.» (مصنف عبد الرزاق 16514). عَنِ ابْنِ شُبْرُمَةَ: «إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مَا وَهَبَ لَهُ صَاحِبُهُ فَلَيْسَ بِشَيْءٍ.» (مصنف عبد الرزاق 16570). عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ: فَشَدَدْتُ عَلَى الْحِمَارِ فَعَقَرْتُهُ، ثُمَّ جِئْتُ بِهِ وَقَدْ مَاتَ، فَوَقَعُوا فِيهِ يَأْكُلُونَهُ، ثُمَّ إِنَّهُمْ شَكُوا فِي أَكْلِهِمْ إِيَّاهُ وَهُمْ حُرُمٌ، فَرُحْنَا وَخَبَأْتُ الْعَضْدَ مَعِي، فَأَدْرَكْنَا رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَسَأَلْنَاهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، فَقَالَ: مَعَكُمْ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ، فَقُلْتُ: نَعَمْ، فَنَاوَلْتُهُ الْعَضْدَ فَأَكَلَهَا حَتَّى نَفِدَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ. (بخاري 2570). وَدَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ: الْحَدِيثُ فِي هِبَةِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَصْحَابِهِ لِهَوَازِنَ مَا غَنِمُوا مِنْهُمْ وَهُوَ غَيْرُ مَقْسُومٍ. (بخاري 2603). وَالْحَدِيثُ عَنْ سَهْلِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ أُتِيَ بِشَرَابٍ، وَعَنْ يَمِينِهِ غُلَامٌ، وَعَنْ يَسَارِهِ أَشْيَاخٌ، فَقَالَ لِلْغُلَامِ: أَتَأْذَنُ لِي أَنْ أُعْطِيَ هَؤُلَاءِ، فَقَالَ الْغُلَامُ: لَا، فَتَلَّهُ فِي يَدِهِ. (بخاري 2605). وَهِبَةُ الْمُشَاعِ فِي مَا لَا يُقْسَمُ جَائِزَةٌ. وَمَنْ وُهِبَ شِقْصًا مُشَاعًا فَالْهِبَةُ فَاسِدَةٌ فَإِنْ قَسَّمَهُ وَسَلَّمَهُ جَازَ. وَلَوْ وَهَبَ دَقِيقًا فِي حِنْطَةٍ أَوْ دُهْنًا فِي سِمْسِمٍ فَالْهِبَةُ فَاسِدَةٌ فَإِنْ طَحَنَ وَسَلَّمَ لَمْ يَجُزْ. وَإِنْ كَانَتْ الْعَيْنُ الْمَوْهُوبَةُ فِي يَدِ الْمَوْهُوبِ لَهُ مَلَكَهَا بِالْهِبَةِ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يُجَدِّدْ فِيهَا قَبْضًا. وَإِذَا وَهَبَ الْأَبُ لِابْنِهِ الصَّغِيرِ هِبَةً مَلَكَهَا الْإِبْنُ بِالْعَقْدِ فَإِنْ وَهَبَ لَهُ أَجْنَبِيٌّ هِبَةً تَمَّتْ بِقَبْضِ الْأَبِ. وَإِذَا وُهِبَ لِلْيَتِيمِ هِبَةٌ فَقَبَضَهَا لَهُ وَلِيُّهُ جَازَ. عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ: (الْحَدِيثُ السَّابِقُ). عَنِ ابْنِ شُبْرُمَةَ: سَأَلْتُهُ عَنْ شِقْصٍ مُشَاعٍ فَقَالَ: «إِذَا سَمَّى فَجَعَلَ لَهُ مِائَةَ دِينَارٍ مِنْ مَالِهِ فَهُوَ جَائِزٌ، وَإِنْ سَمَّى ثُلُثًا أَوْ رُبُعًا لَمْ يَجُزْ حَتَّى يُقَسَّمَ.» (مصنف عبد الرزاق 16531). عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ: كُنَّا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ في سَفَرٍ وَكُنْتُ عَلَى بَكْرٍ صَعْبٍ فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ لِعُمَرَ: بِعْنِيهِ فَابْتَاعَهُ فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ: هُوَ لَكَ يَا عَبْدَ اللهِ. (بخاري 2611). عَنْ عُثْمَانَ بْنِ عَفَّانَ: «مَنْ نَحَلَ وَلَدًا لَهُ صَغِيرًا لَمْ يَبْلُغْ أَنْ يَكُونَ تَحْلَهُ، فَأَعْلَنَ بِهَا وَأَشْهَدَ عَلَيْهَا، فَهِيَ جَائِزَةٌ وَإِنْ وَلِيَهَا أَبُوهُ.» (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي 11952). عَنْ أَبِي مُوسَى الْأَشْعَرِيِّ قَالَ: قَالَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ: «الْأَنْحَالُ مِيرَاثٌ مَا لَمْ يُقْبَضْ.»
Book of Gifts. And the gift is not valid in what is divisible except taken possession of after division. And the gift is concluded by his saying 'I gifted you' and 'I bestowed upon you'. From Umar: 'I mounted a horse in the path of Allah, then I saw it being sold, so I asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he said: Do not buy it and do not take back your charity.' (Bukhari 2636). From Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz: 'No gift is valid except what is separated, isolated, and made known.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq 16514). From Ibn Shubruma: 'If each of them does not have what his companion gifted him, then it is nothing.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq 16570). From Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father: '...I pressed the donkey and wounded it, then I brought it dead, they fell upon it eating, then they doubted while in ihram, ... so we went and I hid the arm, then we caught the Prophet and asked, he said: Do you have any of it? I said yes, so I gave him the arm and he ate it until it was finished while he was in ihram.' (Bukhari 2570). And the proof of al-Shafi'i: The hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions gifting to Hawazin what they had taken as booty from them while it was undivided. (Bukhari 2603). And the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd: 'The Prophet was brought a drink, on his right a boy, on his left elders, he said to the boy: Do you permit me to give these? The boy said no, so he placed it in his hand.' (Bukhari 2605). And the gift of common ownership in what is not divisible is valid. This passage is a commentary on the matn of al-Quduri regarding the conditions for validity of gifts (hibah). It states rulings and provides proofs from hadith, along with a response to the Shafi'i position. The author first presents the ruling that a gift of divisible property is not valid unless it is taken possession of after division (محوزة مقسومة). Gift of Undivided Share and Commingled Goods
Rulings on gift of undivided share in divisible and indivisible property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gift of undivided shares (mushā‘) and distinguish between divisible and indivisible property, applying the condition of possession (qabd) using the provided hadith and qawl sahabi as evidence.

Core Idea
Gift of an undivided share is valid only in property that cannot be divided; divisible property requires division and delivery.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Kitab al-Hibah addresses a critical nuance in the law of gifts: the validity of gifting an undivided share (mushā‘). The Hanafi ruling hinges on the nature of the property—whether it can be divided without loss or not. The text also provides prophetic and companion evidence to support its position, illustrating a key principle of possession (qabd) in gift contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First, note the ruling for gifting an undivided share in property that cannot be divided (valid). Second, the ruling for gifting an undivided share in divisible property (invalid without division and delivery).
The text also adds a third scenario: gifting commingled goods like flour in wheat or oil in sesame.
2
Understand the underlying legal principle
The validity depends on the possibility of possession (qabd). In indivisible property, possession can be had jointly without physical division. In divisible property, possession of an undivided share is not possible without demarcation.
This is why the gift of an undivided share in divisible property is fasid (invalid) until division and delivery.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith of Abu Qatada shows the Prophet accepting a gift of an entire foreleg (musnad) while in ihram—an undivided share of the animal. This supports the validity of mushā‘ in indivisible property.
The animal was small and could not be divided practically.
4
Analyze the qawl sahabi proof
The saying of Ibn Shubrumah distinguishes between a gift of a specific number of dinars (valid) and a gift of a fraction like one-third (invalid until division). This supports the second ruling.
The fraction is unspecified and requires division to know the exact share.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi‘i school holds that gift of mushā‘ in divisible property is valid because possession can be achieved by mutual permission. Recognize the thamarah (practical effect) in real estate gifts.
This difference is legitimate and based on different definitions of qabd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الهِبَةِ
٥. وَهِبَةُ الْمُشَاعِ فِي مَا لَا يُقْسَمُ جَائِزَةٌ وَمَنْ وُهِبَ شِقْصًا مُشَاعًا فَالْهبةُ فَاسِدَةٌ فَإِنْ قَسَّمَهُ وَسَلَّمَهُ جَازَ وَلَوْ وَهَبَ دَقِيقًا فِي حِنْطَةٍ أَوْ دُهْنَا فِي سِمْسِم فَالْهبةُ فَاسِدَةً فَإِنْ طَحَنَ وَسَلَّمَ لَمْ يَجُزْ 
توجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَهِبَةُ الْمُشَاعِ فِي مَا لَا يُقْسَمُ جَائِزَةٌ 
عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ السَّلَمِيِّ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ ..... فَشَدَدْتُ عَلَى الْحِمَارِ فَعَقَرْتُهُ، ثُمَّ جِئْتُ بِهِ وَقَدْ مَاتَ، فَوَقَعُوا فِيهِ يَأْكُلُونَهُ، ثُمَّ إِنَّهُمْ شَكُوا فِي أَكْلِهِمْ إِيَّاهُ وَهُمْ حُرُمٌ، فَرُحْنَا وَخَبَأْتُ الْعَضْدَ مَعِي، فَأَدْرَكْنَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَسَأَلْنَاهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، فَقَالَ : مَعَكُمْ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ، فَقُلْتُ: نَعَمْ، فَنَاوَلْتُهُ الْعَضْدَ فَأَكَلَهَا حَتَّى نَفِدَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ.» (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ مَنِ اسْتَوْهَبَ مِنْ أَصْحَابِهِ شَيْئًا، نمبر 2570)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ وُهِبَ شِقْصًا مُشَاعًا فَالْهبةُ فَاسِدَةٌ 
سَأَلْتُ ابْنَ شُبْرُمَةَ عَنْهُ فَقَالَ: «إِذَا سَمَّى فَجَعَلَ لَهُ مِائَةَ دِينَارٍ مِنْ مَالِهِ فَهُوَ جَائِزٌ، وَإِنْ سَمَّى ثُلُثًا أَوْ رُبُعًا لَمْ يَجُزْ حَتَّى يُقَسَّمَهُ»، مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ الْهِبَاتِ، نمبر 16531)
Book of Gifts. 5. The gift of an undivided share in what cannot be divided is valid. And whoever is given an undivided share, the gift is invalid. If he divides it and hands it over, it becomes valid. And if he gives flour in wheat or oil in sesame, the gift is invalid; if he grinds and hands over, it is not valid. Attention: (1) The hadith to establish: 'Gift of undivided share in what cannot be divided is valid' from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada... (2) The saying of a Tabi‘i to establish: 'And whoever is given an undivided share, the gift is invalid'...
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Hibah of al-Quduri presents rulings on the gift of undivided shares (mushā‘). The first ruling states that gifting an undivided share in property that is indivisible by nature (such as a small animal or a well) is valid. However, if the property is divisible, such as land or a house, gifting an undivided share is invalid unless the donor divides the property and delivers the specific portion. The text then gives an example: gifting a quantity of flour within wheat, or oil within sesame seeds, is invalid because the flour/oil is commingled and undivided; even if the donor grinds the wheat to separate the flour or presses the sesame for oil, the gift does not become valid because the donee does not receive a specific share. This follows the Hanafi principle that a gift requires both offer and acceptance, but for validity, possession (qabd) is necessary, and possession of an undivided share in divisible property is not possible without division. The proofs provided are a hadith from Abu Qatada about accepting a gift of a hunted animal while in ihram, and a saying of Ibn Shubrumah that a gift of a specific number of dinars is valid, but a fraction (like one-third) is not until divided.

Key Terms
المشاع (al-mushā‘): Undivided share in jointly owned property; a share not separated by demarcation.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession; delivery of the gifted item from donor to donee, a condition for gift completion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is a gift of an undivided share (mushā‘) valid without division?
A) When the property is divisible, like land
B) When the property is indivisible by nature, like a small animal
C) When the donor grinds or processes the item
D) When the donee is a relative

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a gift of an undivided share is valid only if the property is indivisible by nature; otherwise, division and delivery are mandatory.

Gift Valid Without Renewed Possession When Object Already Held
Ruling valid gift without renewed possession if object already held by donee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a gift when the gifted item is already in the donee’s possession, identify the proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i requirement of new possession.

Core Idea
Existing possession satisfies the qabd requirement — the gift is complete by contract alone.

The Hanafi school recognizes a practical exception to the general rule that a gift requires the donee to take possession (qabd). If the gifted item is already under the donee's control, such as a borrowed or deposited item, the gift becomes valid immediately upon the offer and acceptance, without any physical transfer. This lesson examines the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The donee already holds the gifted item (e.g., as a borrower or depositary).
The item is physically under the donee's control before the gift contract.
2
State the ruling
The gift is valid (sahih) and ownership transfers immediately, even if no new possession (qabd) occurs.
The contract of gift (ijab + qabul) is sufficient.
3
Examine the textual proof
The hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet gifted a camel while Ibn Umar was riding it, indicating no separate transfer needed.
The hadith is from Bukhari (no. 2611) and is used as a direct proof.
4
Understand the legal implication
The principle: pre-existing possession fulfills the qabd requirement for a gift.
This is unique to the Hanafi school.
5
Contrast with the opposing school
The Shafi'i school holds that new possession (qabd jadid) is required even if the donee already has the item.
The practical difference: immediate ownership vs. delayed until new transfer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَتْ الْعَيْنُ الْمَوْهُوبَةُ فِي يَدِ الْمَوْهُوبِ لَهُ مَلَكَهَا بِالْهبةِ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يُجَدِدْ فِيهَا قَبْضًا 
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ كَانَتْ الْعَيْنُ الْمَوْهُوبَةُ 
عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ «كُنَّا مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في سَفَرٍ وَكُنْتُ عَلَى بَكْرٍ صَعْب فَقَالَ النَّبِي صلى الله عليه وسلم لِعُمَرَ بِعْنِيهِ فَابْتَاعَهُ فَقَالَ النَّبِي صلى الله عليه وسلم هُوَ لَكَ يَا عَبْدَ اللهِ.» (بخاري شريف بَابٌ : إِذَا وَهَبَ بَعِيرًا لِرَجُلٍ وَهُوَ رَاكِبُهُ فَهُوَ جَائِزٌ، نمبر 2611)
And if the gifted property is in the hand of the donee, he owns it by the gift, even if he does not renew possession in it. Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish: ... from Ibn Umar...
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage addresses a common scenario: the donee already has the gifted item in his possession, e.g., a borrowed item or a deposit. The ruling states that no new physical possession (qabd) is required; the gift is valid simply by the contract. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet gave him a camel that Ibn Umar was already riding. The Prophet said, 'It is yours, O Abdullah.' Since the camel was already under Ibn Umar's control, the gift was complete without a separate act of taking. This is unique to the Hanafi school; other schools may require a symbolic transfer.

Key Terms
الموهوب له (al-mawhūb lahu): The recipient of the gift (donee).
قبض (qabd): Physical possession or taking of an item; in gifts, a condition for validity unless pre-existing possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person already has an item in his possession (e.g., a borrowed book) and the owner says 'I gift it to you', when does the donee own it according to the Hanafi school?
A) Immediately, without new possession
B) Only after physically handing it back and taking it again
C) Only after one year
D) Never, because a gift requires the donor to physically give

Key Takeaway
If the gifted item is already in the donee's hand, ownership transfers by the gift contract alone; no new possession is needed.

Gift to Minors and Orphans: Possession by Guardian
Rulings on gifts to minors and orphans and who may take possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gifts to minors and identify the conditions under which possession is required.

Core Idea
Father's gift to minor son vests by contract alone; a stranger's gift requires guardian's possession.

In Hanafi law, gifts to minors are treated differently depending on who gives them. This lesson examines the key ruling: when a father gifts his minor child, ownership transfers immediately by contract. However, if a stranger gives, the child's property right only completes when the guardian takes possession. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct application of gift transactions involving children.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Giving a gift to a minor. What is the ruling? It is valid, but ownership vests immediately only when the donor is the father.
The father is treated as an extension of the child in property matters.
2
Locate the dalil
What proofs does the author cite? Sayings of Uthman, Umar, and a tabi'i from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
These are considered strong evidence in the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each proof show that father's gift is immediate? Uthman's statement indicates that the father's gift is valid even though he manages it. Umar's saying implies that gifts are like inheritance until possession is taken, but the father's gift is an exception.
The key phrase is 'فهي جائزة وإن وليها أبوه' – the gift is valid even if the father handles it.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Which schools disagree? Others (e.g., Shafi'i) require possession for all gifts. The Hanafi response: father's guardianship justifies the exception. The Hanafi position is relied upon for fatwa.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, Hanafi law considers the father's gift final immediately, while Shafi'i law requires the father to take possession on the child's behalf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا وَهَبَ الْأَبُ لِابْنِهِ الصَّغِيرِ هِبَةً مَلَكَهَا الإِبْنُ بِالْعَقْدِ فَإِنْ وَهَبَ لَهُ أَجْنَبِيٌّ هِبَةً تَمَّتْ بِقَبْضِ الْأَبِ وَإِذَا وُهِبَ لِلْيَتِيمِ هِبَةٌ فَقَبَضَهَا لَهُ وَلِيُّهُ جَازَ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي حِجْرِ أُمِّهِ فَقَبْضُهَا لَهُ جَائِزٌ 
ووجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا وَهَبَ الْأَبُ لِابْنِهِ الصَّغِيرِ هِبَةً 
عَنْ عُثْمَانَ بْنِ عَفَّانَ أَنَّهُ قَالَ : " مَنْ نَحَلَ وَلَدًا لَهُ صَغِيرًا لَمْ يَبْلُغْ أَنْ يَكُونَ تَحْتَهُ، فَأَعْلَنَ بِهَا وَأَشْهَدَ عَلَيْهَا، فَهِيَ جَائِزَةٌ وَإِنْ وَلِيَهَا أَبُوهُ " ، (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ يَقْبِضُ لِلطِّفْلِ أَبُوهُ، نمبر 11952)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا وَهَبَ الْأَبُ لِابْنِهِ الصَّغِيرِ هِبَةً 
عَنْ أَبِي مُوسَى الْأَشْعَرِيِّ قَالَ : قَالَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ : " الأَنْحَالُ مِيرَاثٌ مَا لَمْ يُقْبَضْ " وَرُوِّينَا عَنْ عُثْمَانَ وَابْنِ عُمَرَ وَابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ شَرْطِ الْقَبْض في الهبة، نمبر 11951)
وجه (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا وَهَبَ الْأَبُ لِابْنِهِ الصَّغِيرِ هِبَةً 
قَالَ: فَشُكِيَ ذَلِكَ إِلَى عُثْمَانَ فَرَأَى أَنَّ الْوَالِدَ يَجُوزُ لِوَلَدِهِ إِذَا كَانُوا صِغَارًا (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ يَقْبِضُ لِلطِّفْلِ أَبُوهُ، نمبر 11954)
And if the father gives a gift to his minor son, the son owns it by the contract. If a stranger gives a gift to him, it is completed by the father's possession. And if a gift is given to an orphan, and his guardian takes possession for him, it is valid. And if the child is under the care of his mother, her possession for him is valid. Evidence: (1) Saying of companion Uthman... (2) Saying of companion Umar... (3) Saying of tabi‘i...
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This set of rulings concerns gifts to minors. The Hanafi school gives the father a special status: when he gifts something to his minor child, ownership transfers immediately by the contract alone, without need for physical possession, because the father's dominion over the child's property is recognized. However, if a non-relative gives a gift to a minor, it does not become the child's property until the father (or guardian) takes physical possession on the child's behalf. Similarly, for an orphan, the guardian's possession completes the gift. The text adds that if the child is in the care of his mother, her possession for him is valid, as the mother is a de facto guardian. The proofs include sayings of Uthman and Umar that gifts to minors are valid when the father takes possession, and that gifts are inheritance-like until possession is taken.

Key Terms
وليّ (walī): Guardian; the father, grandfather, or executor who manages the minor's affairs. In this lesson, the wali takes possession of a gift on behalf of the minor.
هبة (hiba): Gift; transfer of ownership without exchange of consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A stranger gives a gift to a minor child. According to the Hanafi school, when does the child own the gift?
A) Immediately by the contract
B) After the father takes possession on the child's behalf
C) Only when the child reaches puberty
D) Only if the mother is present

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a father's gift to his minor child is effective immediately by contract; all other gifts to minors require possession by the guardian.

Gift by One to Two or Two to One
Intra-Hanafi dispute on gift by one person to two donees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on gifting one property to two donees and identify the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
One donor to two donees: Abu Hanifa says invalid; Sahibayn allow it. The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa.

Gifting a single undivided property to two people simultaneously raises a question about possession. While gifting from two donors to one donee is unanimously valid, the reverse case creates a dispute within the Hanafi school. This lesson examines the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, along with their respective proofs from hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed scenario
Note that when two donors give a house to one donee, the gift is valid by consensus. This is because each donor gives his own separate share, and possession is clear.
2
State the disputed scenario
When one donor gives a house to two donees, there is an ikhtilaf. Recall that Abu Hanifa rules it invalid (fasid), while Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule it valid (sahih).
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's evidence
Abu Hanifa relies on the saying of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz that no gift is valid unless separated and known (مصنف عبد الرزاق). He also analogises that giving an undivided share of a divisible property is invalid, so giving the whole to two cannot be valid.
The hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd about the Prophet giving a drink to one boy is also cited as evidence for giving to one only.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's evidence
The Sahibayn cite the practice of Asma' bint Abi Bakr who gave a property to two persons (Qasim and Ibn Abi 'Atiq) without division. They also argue that the Prophet's action of giving a drink to one boy from a group does not prohibit giving to multiple donees.
The Sahibayn consider joint possession feasible through mutual cooperation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the gift is void until the donor divides the property and delivers specific portions; under Sahibayn, the donees become joint owners immediately. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view for precaution.
Al-Quduri presents Abu Hanifa's opinion first, indicating it is the relied-upon madhhab position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ وَهَبَ اثْنَانِ لِوَاحِدٍ دَارًا جَازَ وَإِنْ وَهَبَهَا وَاحِدٌ مِنْ اثْنَيْنِ لَمْ يَجُزْ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَصِحُ 
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ وَهَبَ اثْنَانِ لِوَاحِدٍ دَارًا جَازَ 
عَنْ سَهْلِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ : «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أُتِيَ بِشَرَابِ فَشَرِبَ ...: مَا كُنْتُ لِأُوثِرَ بِنَصِيبي مِنْكَ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ أَحَدًا، فَتَلَّهُ فِي يَدِهِ.»، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ هِبَةِ الْوَاحِدِ لِلْجَمَاعَةِ، نمبر 2602)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ وَهَبَهَا وَاحِدٌ مِنْ اثْنَيْنِ لَمْ يَجُزْ 
قَالَ: كَتَبَ عُمَرُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ «أَنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ مِنَ النُّحْلِ إِلَّا مَا عُزِلَ وَأُفْرِدَ وَأُعْلِمَ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ النُّحْلِ،نمبر 16514)
وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ وَهَبَهَا وَاحِدٌ مِنْ اثْنَيْنِ لَمْ يَجُزْ 
سَأَلْتُ ابْنَ شُبْرُمَةَ عَنْهُ فَقَالَ: «إِذَا سَمَّى فَجَعَلَ لَهُ مِائَةَ دِينَارٍ مِنْ مَالِهِ فَهُوَ جَائِزٌ، وَإِنْ سَمَّى ثُلُثًا أَوْ رُبُعًا لَمْ يَجُزْ حَتَّى يُقَسَّمَهُ»، مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ الْهِبَاتِ، نمبر 16531)
وجه (۱) دليل الصاحبين قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ وَهَبَهَا وَاحِدٌ مِنْ اثْنَيْنِ لَمْ يَجُزْ 
وَقَالَتْ أَسْمَاءُ لِلْقَاسِمِ بْنِ مُحَمَّدٍ وَابْنِ أَبِي عَتِيقٍ: «وَرِثْتُ عَنْ أُخْتِي عَائِشَةَ بِالْغَابَةِ وَقَدْ أَعْطَانِي بِهِ مُعَاوِيَةُ مِائَةَ أَلْفٍ فَهُوَ لَكُمَا.»، بخاري شريف، بَابُ هِبَةِ الْوَاحِدِ لِلْجَمَاعَةِ، نمبر 2602
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ وَهَبَهَا وَاحِدٌ مِنْ اثْنَيْنِ لَمْ يَجُزْ 
عَنْ سَهْلِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ : «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ أُتِي بِشَرَابٍ فَشَرِبَ، وَعَنْ يَمِينِهِ غُلَامٌ، وَعَنْ يَسَارِهِ الأَشْيَاخُ، فَقَالَ لِلْغُلَامٍ: إِنْ أَذِنْتَ لِي أَعْطَيْتُ هَؤُلَاءِ، فَقَالَ: مَا كُنْتُ لِأُوثِرَ بِنَصِيبي مِنْكَ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ أَحَدًا، فَتَلَّهُ فِي يَدِهِ.» (بخاري شريف، بَابُ هِبَةِ الْوَاحِدِ لِلْجَمَاعَةِ، نمبر 2602)
And if two persons give a house to one, it is valid. And if one person gives it to two, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is valid. Evidence: (1) Hadith from Sahl ibn Sa‘d: ... (2) Saying of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz: 'No gift is valid unless it is separated, singled out, and known.' (3) Saying of Ibn Shubrumah... (4) Evidence of the two companions: saying of Asma' bint Abi Bakr: 'I inherited from my sister Aisha a property... it is for you two.' (5) Hadith from Sahl ibn Sa‘d (similar).
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about gifting one thing to multiple donees. The case: two donors give a house to one donee – this is unanimously valid because each donor gives his own share. But if one donor gives a house to two donees, Imam Abu Hanifa deems the gift invalid because the gift is one undivided thing given to two persons, and possession by both cannot be realized simultaneously without division. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold it valid, as the gift can be completed by each taking possession of his share through mutual cooperation. The proofs cited: a hadith where the Prophet gave his drink to a boy (one donee) after the boy refused to let him give to others, indicating validity of giving to one. For the Sahibayn, the practice of Asma' gifting a property to two people is cited. Also, the saying of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz that gifts must be separated supports Abu Hanifa's view. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn's view is also considered strong. Practical consequence: if someone gifts a house to two men, the gift is invalid per Abu Hanifa, so they do not own it until division; according to the Sahibayn, the gift is valid and they own it jointly.

Key Terms
النُّحْلُ (al-nuḥl): Gift (synonym for hibah), often used for gifts to family.
فَاسِد (fāsid): Voidable; an act that is not inherently prohibited but lacks a condition for validity. In this context, the gift is not completely void (bāṭil) but invalid unless the condition of separation is fulfilled.
قَبْض (qabḍ): Taking possession; a condition for the completion of a gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa when one person gives a house to two people without specifying shares?
A) Valid; they become co-owners
B) Invalid until the house is divided and each receives a specific portion
C) Valid only if the donees are relatives
D) Invalid unconditionally, even after division

Key Takeaway
A gift by one donor to multiple donees is invalid according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position unless the property is divided and each donee takes separate possession.

Gift to Mahram Relative and Spouse: No Right of Return
States ruling that gifts to mahram and spouses are irrevocable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on revocation of gifts to mahram relatives and spouses, and identify the operative difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Gifts to mahram relatives and between spouses are irrevocable in the Hanafi school.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling from Kitab al-Hibah: the irrevocability of gifts given to certain categories. While gifts can normally be revoked under certain conditions, the Hanafi school carves out two exceptions to preserve family and marital bonds. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing the categories of donees where revocation is permanently barred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Find in the text the two types of donees for whom gifts become irrevocable: (1) a mahram relative (dhi rahim mahram), and (2) a spouse (one of the spouses gifting to the other).
Mahram includes all blood and foster relatives whom one cannot marry.
2
Understand the legal effect
The phrase 'fala ruju'a fiha' (there is no return in it) means the donor permanently loses the right to revoke or reclaim the gifted item. This is a binding prohibition.
The general rule allows revocation before possession, but this is an exception.
3
Distinguish the exception from the general rule
Recall that in Hanafi fiqh, a donor usually may revoke a gift before the donee takes possession, and in some cases even after. Here, revocation is completely barred, regardless of possession.
The exception is based on preserving family and marital bonds.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi‘i allows revocation for mahram relatives except parents and children. Understand that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
Knowing this helps in comparative fiqh discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ وَهَبَ هِبَةً لِذِي رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهُ فَلَا رُجُوعَ فِيهَا وَكَذَلِكَ مَا وَهَبَهُ أَحَدُ الزَّوْجَيْنِ لِلْآخَرِ
And if he gives a gift to a mahram relative from him, then there is no return in it. And similarly, what one of the spouses gifted to the other.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from Kitab al-Hibah. It establishes two categories of gifts that are irrevocable: (1) a gift given to a mahram relative (one who is permanently prohibited for marriage), and (2) a gift between spouses. The right of return (ruju‘) that a donor normally has (under certain conditions) is completely negated in these cases. The wisdom is to preserve family bonds and marital harmony. The ruling is based on hadith and the practice of the Salaf.

Key Terms
ذِي رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ (dhi rahim mahram): A relative who is permanently forbidden for marriage due to blood relationship or fosterage.
الرُّجُوعُ (al-ruju‘): The donor's legal right to take back the gifted item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, at any time.
B) Yes, but only with her consent.
C) No, it cannot be revoked.
D) No, unless the gift is still in his possession.

Key Takeaway
Gifts to mahram relatives and between spouses are irrevocable in the Hanafi school, with a legitimate ikhtilaf from the Shafi‘i school.

Compensation and the Right to Revoke a Gift
Rules on compensation and its effect on gift revocation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which compensation ('iwad) extinguishes the donor's right to revoke a gift and distinguish between compensation offered by the donee versus a third party.

Core Idea
Accepting compensation for a gift cancels the right to revoke — but only with explicit wording and voluntary consent.

In Hanafi gift law, a donor typically can revoke a gift unless compensation is given. This lesson explores when compensation extinguishes that right. We will examine the specific wording required and the effect of compensation from a third party.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal effect
The donor takes compensation ('iwad) from the donee or a third party. The ruling is that the right to revoke (ruju') drops. Note that the compensation must be explicit.
The text uses 'خُذْ هَذَا عِوَضًا' or similar phrases.
2
Confirm the condition of explicit wording
The donee must use specific words: 'عِوَضًا', 'بَدَلًا', or 'فِي مُقَابَلَتِهَا'. Compensation without such formulation does not extinguish the right.
These terms indicate the intention of exchange.
3
Distinguish between donee and stranger compensation
If a stranger (ajnabi) voluntarily gives compensation on behalf of the donee, and the donor accepts, the right also drops. The donee's consent is not required.
The stranger's compensation is valid even without the donee's request.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا قَالَ الْمَوْهُوبُ لَهُ لِلْوَاهِبِ خُذْ هَذَا عِوَضًا عَنْ هِبَتِكَ أَوْ بَدَلًا مِنْهَا أَوْ فِي مُقَابَلَتِهَا فَقَبَضَهُ الْوَاهِبُ سَقَطَ الرُّجُوعُ وَإِنْ عَوَّضَهُ أَجْنَبِيٌّ عَنِ الْمَوْهُوبِ لَهُ مُتَبَرِّعًا فَقَبَضَ الْعِوَضَ سَقَطَ الرُّجُوعُ وَإِذَا اسْتَحَقَّ نِصْفَ الْهِبَةِ رَجَعَ بِنِصْفِ الْعِوَضِ وَإِنِ اسْتَحَقَّ نِصْفَ الْعِوَضِ لَمْ يَرْجِعْ فِي الْهِبَةِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَرُدَّ مَا بَقِيَ مِنَ الْعِوَضِ ثُمَّ يَرْجِعَ فِي الْهِبَةِ وَلَا يَصِحُّ الرُّجُوعُ إِلَّا بِتَرَاضِيهِمَا أَوْ بِحُكْمِ الْحَاكِمِ
And if the donee says to the donor: 'Take this as compensation for your gift, or as a substitute for it, or in exchange for it,' and the donor takes possession of it, the right of return drops. And if a stranger compensates him on behalf of the donee voluntarily, and he (the donor) takes possession of the compensation, the right of return drops. And if half of the gift is reclaimed (by a rightful owner), he returns half of the compensation; and if half of the compensation is reclaimed, he does not return in the gift unless he returns what remains of the compensation, then he returns in the gift. And the return is not valid except by mutual consent or by a judge's ruling.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on how compensation ('iwad) affects the donor's right to revoke a gift. Several scenarios are presented: (1) If the donee offers something as compensation (using explicit words like 'iwad, badal, or fi muqabil), and the donor accepts it, the right of return is lost. (2) Similarly, if a third party (ajnabi) voluntarily gives compensation on behalf of the donee, and the donor accepts, the right is also lost. (3) If it later turns out that half of the gifted property belongs to someone else (istihqaq), the donor can only take back half of the compensation (since half the gift was invalid). (4) If half of the compensation is reclaimed, the donor cannot revoke the gift unless he first returns the remaining compensation to the donee. (5) Finally, any revocation (ruju‘) of a gift (where allowed) requires mutual consent or a court order. The madhhab emphasizes that compensation, once accepted, signifies satisfaction and extinguishes the right to revoke.

Key Terms
عِوَضًا (‘iwadan): Compensation or exchange given in return for the gift.
أَجْنَبِيٌّ (ajnabiyyun): A stranger who is not the donee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following words, when used by the donee, would NOT extinguish the donor's right to revoke?
A) عِوَضًا ('iwadan)
B) بَدَلًا (badalan)
C) شُكْرًا (shukran)
D) فِي مُقَابَلَتِهَا (fi muqabilatiha)

Key Takeaway
Compensation ('iwad) extinguishes the donor's right to revoke a gift only when offered with explicit wording and taken into possession, including when voluntarily given by a stranger.

Partial Reclaim of Gift or Compensation and Requirements for Revocation
Rules on partial reclaim and conditions for valid return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules of partial reclaim (istihqaq) to calculate the donor's restitution rights and state the conditions for a valid return of a gift.

Core Idea
When half a gift is reclaimed, you only get half the compensation back; but when half the compensation is reclaimed, you must return the remainder before revoking.

The previous lesson covered when compensation extinguishes the right to revoke. Now we examine what happens if the gift or compensation is partially reclaimed by a rightful owner. The text provides precise rules for these scenarios and concludes with the general requirement for any valid return: mutual consent or court order.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first partial reclaim scenario
If half of the gifted property is reclaimed (istihaqq) by a third party, the donor is only entitled to take back half of the compensation. This is because the gift was partially invalid.
The text says: 'وَإِذَا اسْتَحَقَّ نِصْفَ الْهِبَةِ رَجَعَ بِنِصْفِ الْعِوَضِ'
2
Understand the second partial reclaim scenario
If half of the compensation is reclaimed, the donor cannot revoke the gift unless he first returns the remaining compensation to the donee. This prevents the donor from gaining unfairly.
The text says: 'وَإِنِ اسْتَحَقَّ نِصْفَ الْعِوَضِ لَمْ يَرْجِعْ فِي الْهِبَةِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَرُدَّ مَا بَقِيَ مِنَ الْعِوَضِ'
3
Recognize the condition for any return
Revocation (ruju') is only valid through mutual consent of both parties or by a judge's ruling. This upholds stability in transactions.
The text ends: 'وَلَا يَصِحُّ الرُّجُوعُ إِلَّا بِتَرَاضِيهِمَا أَوْ بِحُكْمِ الْحَاكِمِ'

This passage is a detailed ruling on how compensation ('iwad) affects the donor's right to revoke a gift. Several scenarios are presented: (1) If the donee offers something as compensation (using explicit words like 'iwad, badal, or fi muqabil), and the donor accepts it, the right of return is lost. (2) Similarly, if a third party (ajnabi) voluntarily gives compensation on behalf of the donee, and the donor accepts, the right is also lost. (4) If half of the compensation is reclaimed, the donor cannot revoke the gift unless he first returns the remaining compensation to the donee. (5) Finally, any revocation (ruju‘) of a gift (where allowed) requires mutual consent or a court order. Gift Perishes or Reclaimed: No Recourse Against Donor
Ruling statement: after gift transfer, donee bears all risk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that the donee has no recourse against the donor when the gifted item perishes or is reclaimed by a rightful owner, and apply it to determine liability in gift transactions.

Core Idea
Once a gift is transferred, the donee bears all risk — no claim back to the donor.

This short ruling from al-Quduri settles a crucial point in gift transactions: after the donee takes possession, the gift is at his risk. If it is destroyed or a third party proves ownership, the donee cannot demand compensation from the donor. Understanding this principle clarifies the transfer of liability in hibah (gift).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The gifted object either perishes (talifat) or is legally claimed by a third party (istahaqqa). The donee is held liable (damina) to compensate the rightful owner in the claim scenario.
2
Determine the consequence for the donee
The donee does not have recourse (lã yarji‘u) to the donor for any compensation. The loss or liability lies entirely with the donee.
3
Recognize the principle
Possession transfers risk. The donor’s responsibility ends once the gift is delivered and accepted by the donee.
This aligns with the Hanafi rule that the donor is only liable for defects existing before the gift, not for subsequent events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا تَلِفَتِ الْعَيْنُ الْمَوْهُوبَةُ أَوِ اسْتَحَقَّهَا مُسْتَحِقٌ فَضَمِنَ الْمَوْهُوبُ لَهُ لَمْ يَرْجِعْ عَلَى الْوَاهِبِ بِشَيْءٍ
And if the gifted object perishes or is claimed by a rightful owner, and the donee is liable (for the value), he does not have recourse against the donor for anything.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This is a ruling about the consequences after a gift has been given and accepted. If the gifted item is destroyed (talafat) while in the donee's possession, or if a third party proves ownership (istahaqqa) and the donee is held liable to compensate that rightful owner (damana), the donee cannot then turn around and demand compensation from the donor. The donor's liability ends once possession is transferred. The donee bears the risk of loss and the risk of legal defects. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that the donor is only responsible for defects existing before the gift was given, but not for subsequent events.

Key Terms
تَلِفَتِ الْعَيْنُ الْمَوْهُوبَةُ (talifat al-‘ayn al-mawhubah): The gifted item is destroyed or lost.
ضَمِنَ (damina): The donee is held liable to pay compensation (e.g., to the rightful owner).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He has no recourse.
C) Only if the donor caused the destruction.
D) He can return the gift and get compensation.

Key Takeaway
The donee assumes all risk of the gifted item after possession; loss or third-party ownership claims do not revert liability to the donor.

Gift with Condition of Compensation Treated as Sale
Definition and ruling of hibah bi-shart al-‘iwad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for validity of a gift with condition of compensation and identify the three sale-like consequences that follow once the contract is perfected.

Core Idea
A gift with condition of compensation is legally a sale: mutual possession is required for validity.

This lesson explains the legal nature of a gift that is conditional on receiving something in return. Unlike an ordinary gift, this transaction is treated as a sale in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding this distinction is crucial because it determines the conditions for validity, the rights of the parties, and the availability of remedies such as defect return, option of sight, and pre-emption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
Recognize that 'hibah bi-shart al-‘iwad' is a gift given on the condition that the donee provides compensation. It is a commutative contract, not a pure gift.
2
Note the condition for validity
The text states that mutual possession (taqabud) of the two compensations is required. Without possession, the contract is not valid. This is the key difference from a pure gift, which can be valid without possession.
Taqabud means both parties physically receive the items or their equivalent.
3
List the sale-like consequences
Once possession occurs, the contract is perfected and treated as a sale. This gives three specific consequences: (1) the item can be returned if defective, (2) the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yh) applies if the item was unseen, and (3) pre-emption (shuf'ah) is obligatory if the property is real estate.
These are remedies typically available in sale contracts.
4
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that such a gift is valid without possession because it remains a gift with a condition of compensation, not a sale. This difference affects when the contract becomes binding.
Hanafi: possession required. Shafi'i: possession not required for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا وَهَبَ بِشَرْطِ الْعِوَضِ اعْتُبِرَ التَّقَابُضُ فِي الْعِوَضَيْنِ فَإِذَا تَقَابَضَا صَحَّ الْعَقْدُ وَصَارَ فِي حُكْمِ الْبَيْعِ يُرَدُّ بِالْعَيْبِ وَخِيَارِ الرُّؤْيَةِ وَتَجِبُ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ
And if he gives a gift with a condition of compensation, mutual possession of the two compensations is required. So when they mutually take possession, the contract is valid and it becomes in the ruling of a sale; it is returned due to a defect and the option of sight, and pre-emption is obligatory in it.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This ruling defines the legal nature of a gift that is conditional on receiving compensation (hibah bi-shart al-‘iwad). It is not a pure gift but a commutative contract. Therefore, both parties must exchange possession (taqabud) for the contract to be valid. Once possession occurs, the contract is perfected and is treated like a sale (bai‘). This means: (a) if the gifted item has a defect, it can be returned; (b) both parties have the option of sight (khiyar al-ru’yah) – i.e., if they hadn't seen the item before, they can cancel after seeing it; and (c) the right of pre-emption (shuf‘ah) applies to the property (if it is real estate). This is a key distinction from irrevocable gifts like those to mahram or spouses.

Key Terms
بِشَرْطِ الْعِوَضِ (bi-shart al-‘iwad): A gift given on the condition that the donee gives something in return.
خِيَارِ الرُّؤْيَةِ (khiyar al-ru’yah): Option of sight: the buyer/donee can cancel after seeing the item if it does not meet expectations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What right of pre-emption applies to a gift given with condition of compensation?
A) Shuf‘ah applies if the property is real estate.
B) No pre-emption applies.
C) Only if the donor pre-empts.
D) The donee can pre-empt.

Key Takeaway
A gift conditioned on compensation is legally a sale: mutual possession is mandatory, and all sale remedies (defect, option of sight, pre-emption) apply.

'Umra and Ruqba: Life Grants and Conditional Transfers
Rulings on 'umra (life grant) and ruqba (conditional grant)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'umra and ruqba in Hanafi law, state the ruling for each, and identify the key legal differences.

Core Idea
'Umra is a valid life grant to the donee and his heirs; ruqba is void due to uncertainty (gharar).

In Hanafi fiqh, the permissibility of property transfers often hinges on clarity of ownership. Two similar but legally distinct grants are 'umra (life grant) and ruqba (conditional grant). This passage from al-Quduri defines each and states the ruling, highlighting the critical role of uncertainty (gharar) in voiding a transaction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two grants
Recognize 'umra as a grant for life with ownership passing to the donee's heirs after death, and ruqba as a conditional grant where ownership depends on survivorship.
Both are forms of gift (hibah) but with different conditions.
2
State the ruling for each
'Umra is ja'izah (permissible/valid). Ruqba is batilah (void) according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
The ruling is explicit in the text.
3
Understand the reason for voidness
Ruqba is void because the condition of survivorship creates uncertainty (gharar) regarding who will own the property, which invalidates the contract.
Gharar is a key principle in Hanafi contract law.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf disagreed with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad and considered ruqba valid. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that ruqba is void.
This is an example of ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Differentiate practical outcomes
In 'umra, the donee owns the property for life and it passes to his heirs. In ruqba, the property never transfers validly; it remains with the original owner or returns to his estate.
Applying the wrong ruling could cause invalid transfers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْعُمْرَى جَائِزَةٌ لِلْمُعَمَّرِ فِي حَالِ حَيَاتِهِ وَلِوَرَثَتِهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَوْتِهِ وَالرُّقْبَى بَاطِلَةٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ
And 'umra is permissible for the donee during his life and for his heirs after his death. And ruqba is void according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage defines two types of grants: (1) 'Umra: A grant of property (usually a house) for the duration of the donee's life, with the condition that it passes to the donee's heirs after his death. This is valid (ja'izah) – the donee becomes owner for life, and the ownership transfers to his heirs upon his death. (2) Ruqba: A conditional grant where the property goes to whichever of the two parties (grantor or grantee) survives the other. This is void (batilah) according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The text does not mention Abu Yusuf’s view here, but it is known that Abu Yusuf considered ruqba valid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the one given by the majority of the Hanafi school: ruqba is void because it involves uncertainty (gharar) regarding ownership.

Key Terms
الْعُمْرَى (al-‘umra): A life grant: 'I give you this for your life, then to your heirs.'
الرُّقْبَى (al-ruqba): A conditional grant: 'Whichever of us survives gets the property.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the ruling on ruqba?
A) It is permissible.
B) It is void.
C) It is valid only if the donee takes possession.
D) It is valid only for relatives.

Key Takeaway
'Umra is valid because it grants ownership without uncertainty; ruqba is void due to gharar (uncertainty) in the condition of survivorship.

Hibah with Condition of Compensation Becomes Like a Sale
Ruling on hibah with condition of compensation requiring mutual possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on hibah bi-shart al-iwad and identify the conditions and consequences that make it equivalent to a sale.

Core Idea
A gift with a condition of compensation is legally a sale — mutual possession is required.

The classical Hanafi text presents a clear ruling: when a gift is given with a stipulation that the recipient gives something in return, the contract is no longer a pure gift. Instead, it is governed by the laws of sale. This lesson unpacks the conditions and legal effects of this transformation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and its condition
Recognize that this is a hibah (gift) where the donor stipulates that the donee must give compensation (shart al-iwad).
2
Determine the condition for validity
Note that mutual possession (taqābuḍ) of both the gifted item and the compensation is required for the contract to become valid.
Without mutual possession, the contract is not binding.
3
Recognize the legal transformation
Once mutual possession occurs, the contract is valid and is treated as a sale in terms of its legal effects.
The label 'gift' does not change the legal nature.
4
List the sale-like consequences
The contract now carries sale rules: return due to unseen defect (radd bi al-ghaib), option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah), and pre-emption (shuf'ah) apply.
These rights protect the parties in an exchange.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ال وَإِذَا وَهَبَ بِشَرْطِ الْعِوَضِ اُعْتُبِرَ التَّقَابُضُ فِي الْعِوَضَيْنِ فَإِذَا تَقَابَضَا صَحَ الْعَقْدُ وَصَارَ فِي حُكْمِ الْبَيْعِ يُرَدُّ بِالْغَيْبِ وَخِيَارِ الرُّؤْيَةِ وَتَجِبُ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ
And when one gives a gift with a condition of compensation, mutual possession is considered in the two compensations. So when they take possession from each other, the contract becomes valid and it falls under the ruling of a sale: it can be returned due to unseen defect and option of sight, and pre-emption is obligatory therein.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of al-Quduri on hibah with a condition of compensation (hibah bi-shart al-iwad). In such a gift, the donor stipulates that the donee must give something in return. The Hanafi school treats this as a sale in effect: both parties must take possession of their respective compensations. Once mutual possession occurs, the contract is valid and is governed by the laws of sale. Accordingly, the buyer (donee) can return the item due to an unseen defect (al-radd bi al-gha'ib) or the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah), and the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) becomes applicable if the property is real estate. This ruling highlights that the intent of the parties, not the label, determines the legal nature of the transaction.

Key Terms
الهِبَة (al-hibah): A contract that involves giving ownership of an asset without compensation.
شَرْط الْعِوَض (shart al-iwad): A condition in the gift that the donee must give something in return.
التَّقَابُض (al-taqābuḍ): Mutual taking possession of the exchanged items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for a hibah bi-shart al-iwad to be valid according to the Hanafi ruling in this passage?
A) The gift must be delivered first.
B) Mutual possession of both items must occur.
C) The compensation must be equal in value.
D) A written contract is required.

Key Takeaway
A gift with a condition of compensation is legally a sale requiring mutual possession for validity.

The Hanafi Ruling on 'Umra: A Life Grant that Becomes Inheritance
Ruling on 'umra with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'umra and explain why it is a valid permanent gift based on the hadith proof.

Core Idea
'Umra is a valid gift; the property vests in the grantee and passes to his heirs, never returning to the donor.

Many misunderstand 'umra as a temporary life tenancy. However, the Hanafi school, relying on a clear hadith, rules that 'umra is a permanent transfer of ownership. In this lesson, we examine the ruling and the evidence that establishes it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'umra, a gift of property for the grantee's life. The ruling is that it is permissible and vests ownership in the grantee during his life and in his heirs after his death.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is a hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah reported in Muslim and Abu Dawud. The hadith explicitly states that the gift belongs to the grantee and his heirs and does not return to the donor.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لا ترجع إلى الذي أعطاها' (it does not return to the one who gave it) and 'وقع فيه المواريث' (becomes subject to inheritance) clearly indicate that 'umra is a permanent gift, not a temporary loan.
The hadith directly addresses the pre-Islamic practice of reversion.
4
Determine the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts this hadith as evidence for the validity of 'umra as a gift that passes to heirs. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
The Shafi'i school differs if the grantee dies without heirs, but the Hanafi position is based on the apparent meaning of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٢ وَالْعُمْرَى جَائِزَةٌ لِلْمُعَمَّرِ فِي حَالِ حَيَاتِهِ وَلِوَرَثَتِهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَوْتِهِ. وجه : (١) الحديث لثبوت: عن جابر بن عبد الله؛ إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ (أَيُّمَا رَجُلٍ أُعْمِرَ عُمْرَى لَهُ، ولعقبه، فأنها لِلَّذِي أُعْطِيَهَا. لَا تَرْجِعُ إِلَى الَّذِي أَعْطَاهَا. لأنه أعطى عطاء وقعت فيه المواريث)، (مسلم شريف - باب العمرى،نمبر 1625/سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الْعُمْرَى، نمبر 3551)
22. And 'umra is permissible for the grantee during his life and for his heirs after his death. Evidence (1) Hadith for proof: From Jabir ibn Abdullah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Any man who is given a life grant (umra) for himself and his offspring, it belongs to the one to whom it is given. It does not return to the one who gave it, because he gave a gift that becomes subject to inheritance.' (Muslim, Book of 'Umra, no. 1625 / Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter on 'Umra, no. 3551)
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This is a ruling from al-Quduri on 'umra, a type of gift where the donor says, 'I give you this property for your life' (often interpreted as a life tenancy). The Hanafi position, supported by this hadith, is that 'umra is a valid transfer of ownership: the grantee owns the property for his life, and upon his death, it passes to his heirs as part of his estate. The donor cannot reclaim it. The hadith explicitly states that it does not return to the donor. This counteracts the pre-Islamic practice where such grants were considered to revert to the donor on the grantee's death. The ruling ensures that the grant is a true gift.

Key Terms
الْعُمْرَى (al-'umrā): A gift of property for the lifetime of the grantee, often with a stipulation that it is for the grantee's life and then to his heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling on 'umra, what happens to the property after the grantee's death?
A) It returns to the donor unconditionally.
B) It passes to the grantee's heirs.
C) It becomes the property of the state.
D) It is given to charity.

Key Takeaway
'Umra is a valid permanent gift; the property does not revert to the donor.
