كِتَابُ الْغَصْبِ وَعَلَى الْغَاصِبِ رَدُّ الْعَيْنِ الْمَغْصُوبَةِ وَإِنْ ادَّعَى هَلَاكَهَا حَبَسَهُ الْحَاكِمُ حَتَّى يَعْلَمَ أَنَّهَا لَوْ كَانَتْ بَاقِيَةً لَأَظْهَرَهَا ثُمَّ يَقْضِيَ عَلَيْهِ بِبَدَهَا وَالْغَصْبُ فِيمَا يُنْقَلُ وَيُحَوَّلُ
وَإِذَا غَصَبَ عَقَارًا فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ لَمْ يَضْمَنْهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ، وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَضْمَنُهُ وَمَا نَقَصَ بِفِعْلِهِ وَسُكْنَاهُ ضَمِنَهُ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعًا وَإِذَا هَلَكَ الْمَغْصُوبُ فِي يَدِ الْغَاصِبِ بِفِعْلِهِ أَوْ بِغَيْرِ فِعْلِهِ ضَمِنَهُ فَإِنْ نَقَصَ فِي يَدِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ ضَمَانُ النُّقْصَانِ
ه وَمَنْ ذَبَحَ شَاةَ غَيْرِهِ فَمَالِكُهَا بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ ضَمَّنَهُ قِيمَتَهَا وَسَلَّمَهَا إِلَيْهِ، يُبْطِلُ عَامَّةَ مَنَافِعِهِ فَلِمَالِكِهِ أَنْ يُضَمِّنَهُ جَمِيعَ قِيمَتِهِ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَعَلَى الْغَاصِبِ رَدُّ الْعَيْنِ الْمَغْصُوبَةِ \ وَمَنْ أَخَذَ عَصَا أَخِيهِ فَلْيَرُدَّهَا " لَم يَقُلْ ابْنُ بَشَّارٍ : ابْنَ يَزِيدَ وَقَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابُ مَنْ يَأْخُذُ الشَّيْءَ عَلَى الْمِزاح، نمبر 5003)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا غَصَبَ عَقَارًا فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ \ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ زَيْدٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ، قَالَ: «مَنْ أَحْيَا أَرْضًا مَيْتَةً فَهِيَ لَهُ، وَلَيْسَ لِعِرْقٍ ظَالِمٍ حَقٌّ» ،سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ في إِحْيَاءِ الْمَوَاتِ، نمبر 3073/سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا ذُكِرَ فِي إِحْيَاءِ أَرْضِ الْمَوَاتِ، نمبر 1378) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا غَصَبَ عَقَارًا فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ اعَنْ سَالِمٍ ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ هُ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ : مَنْ أَخَذَ مِنَ الْأَرْضِ شَيْئًا بِغَيْرِ حَقَّهِ، خُسِفَ بِهِ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ إِلَى سَبْع أَرَضِينَ»، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ إِثْمِ مَنْ ظَلَمَ شَيْئًا مِنَ الْأَرْضِ، نمبر 2454/
توجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَا نَقَصَ بِفِعْلِهِ وَسُكْنَاهُ ضَمِنَهُ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعًا \ عَنْ أَنَسٍ : «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ عِنْدَ بَعْضٍ نِسَائِهِ، فَأَرْسَلَتْ إِحْدَى أُمَّهَاتِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ مَعَ خَادِمٍ بِقَصْعَةٍ فِيهَا طَعَامٌ، فَضَرَبَتْ بِيَدِهَا فَكَسَرَتِ الْقَصْعَةَ ، فَضَمَّهَا وَجَعَلَ فِيهَا الطَّعَامَ، وَقَالَ: كُلُوا، وَحَبَسَ الرَّسُولَ وَالْقَصْعَةَ حَتَّى فَرَغْوا، فَدَفَعَ الْقَصْعَةَ الصَّحِيحَةَ وَحَبَسَ الْمَكْسُورةَ»،(بخاري شريف، بَابٌ : إِذَا كَسَرَ قَصْعَةً أَوْ شَيْئًا لِغَيْرِهِ، نمبر 2481)
د وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ ذَبَحَ شَاةَ غَيْرِهِ فَمَالِكُهَا بِالْخيَارِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ لله قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «كَانَ رَجُلٌ فِي بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ يُقَالُ لَهُ جُرَيْجٌ يُصَلِّي ..... فَأَتَوْهُ وَكَسَرُوا صَوْمَعَتَهُ
اصول : غاصب کے پاس عین مغصوب موجود ہو تو عین مغصوب ہی کو واپس کرنا واجب ہو گا۔
وَإِنْ شَاءَ ضَمَّنَهُ نُقْصَانَهَا وَمَنْ خَرَقَ ثَوْبَ غَيْرِهِ خَرْقًا يَسِيرًا ضَمِنَ نُقْصَانَهُ وَإِنْ خَرَقَهُ خَرْقًا كَثِيرًا ل وَإِذَا تَغَيَّرَتْ الْعَيْنُ الْمَغْصُوبَةُ بِفِعْلِ الْغَاصِبِ حَتَّى زَالَ اسْمُهَا وَعُظْمَ مَنَافِعِهَا زَالَ مِلْكُ الْمَغْصُوبِ مِنْهُ عَنْهَا وَمَلَكَهَا الْغَاصِبُ وَضَمِنَهَا إلَى آخِرِهِ وَلَمْ يَحِلَّ لَهُ الِانْتِفَاعُ بِمَا حَتَّى يُؤَدِّيَ بَدَهَا وَإِنْ غَصَبَ فِضَّةَ أَوْ ذَهَبًا فَضَرَبَهَا دَرَاهِمَ أَوْ دَنَانِيرَ أَوْ آنِيَةً لَمْ يَزُلْ مِلْكُ مَالِكِهَا عَنْهَا عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا سَبِيلَ لِلْمَغْصُوبِ مِنْهُ عَلَى الدَّرَاهِم وَالدَّنَانِيرِ الْمَضْرُوبَةِ وَعَلَيْهِ مِثْلُ الْفِضَّةِ الَّتِي غَصَبَهَا وَمَلَكَهَا الْغَاصِبُ
ك وَمَنْ غَصَبَ سَاجَةً فَبَنَى عَلَيْهَا زَالَ مِلْكُ مَالِكِهَا عَنْهَا وَلَوْمَ الْغَاصِبَ قِيمَتُهَا فَأَنْزَلُوهُ وَسَبُوهُ ، فَتَوَضَّأَ وَصَلَّى ثُمَّ أَتَى الْغُلَامَ فَقَالَ : مَنْ أَبُوكَ يَا غُلَامُ قَالَ: الرَّاعِي، قَالُوا : نَبْنِي صَوْمَعَتَكَ مِنْ ذَهَبٍ، قَالَ : لا ، إِلا مِنْ طِين. » بخاري شريف بَابٌ : إِذَاكَسَرَ قَصْعَةً أَوْ شَيْئًا لِغَيْرِهِ، 2482) توجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا تَغَيَّرَتْ الْعَيْنُ الْمَغْصُوبَةُ \ أَخْبَرَنَا عَاصِمُ بْنُ كُلَيْبِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ رَجُلٍ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ، قَالَ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي جَنَازَةِ، فَرَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَهُوَ عَلَى الْقَبْرِ يُوصِي الْحَافِرَ: «أَوْسِعْ مِنْ قِبَلِ رِجْلَيْهِ، أَوْسِعْ مِنْ قِبَلِ رَأْسِهِ»، فَلَمَّا رَجَعَ اسْتَقْبَلَهُ دَاعِي امْرَأَةٍ فَجَاءَ وَجِيءَ بِالطَّعَامِ فَوَضَعَ يَدَهُ، ثُمَّ وَضَعَ الْقَوْمُ، فَأَكَلُوا، فَنَظَرَ آبَاؤُنَا رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَلُوكُ لُقْمَةً فِي فَمِهِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «أَجِدُ لَحْمَ شَاةٍ أُخِذَتْ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ أَهْلِهَا»، فَأَرْسَلَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ، قَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنِّي أَرْسَلْتُ إِلَى الْبَقِيع يَشْتَرِي لي شَاةً، فَلَمْ أَجِدْ فَأَرْسَلْتُ إِلَى جَارٍ لي قَدِ اشْتَرَى شَاةً أَنْ أَرْسِلْ إِلَيَّ بِمَا بِثَمَنِهَا، فَلَمْ يُوجَدْ، فَأَرْسَلْتُ إِلَى امْرَأَتِهِ فَأَرْسَلَتْ إِلَيَّ بِمَا، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أَطْعِمِيهِ الْأُسَارَى»، سنن ابوداود شریف، بَابٌ فِي اجْتِتَابِ الشُّبُهَاتِ، نمبر 3332 سنن دارقطني، الصَّيْدِ وَالدَّبَائِحِ وَالْأَطْعِمَةِ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ، غمبر 4763)
ى وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ غَصَبَ سَاجَةً فَبَنَى عَلَيْهَا \ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ زَيْدٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، قَالَ: «مَنْ أَحْيَا أَرْضًا مَيْتَةً فَهِيَ لَهُ ، وَلَيْسَ لِعِرْقٍ ظَالِمٍ حَقٌّ»، سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي إِحْيَاءِ الْمَوَاتِ، اصول: امام ابو حنیفہ : مغصوب شی میں تبدیلی آجائے تو غاصب اس کا مالک بن جاتا ہے، لیکن اسکا ضمان لازم ہو گا، ا اور ضمان کی ادائیگی سے قبل استفادہ حلال نہ ہو گا، بر خلاف امام شافعی کے۔
اصول شی مغصوب کی واپسی سے غاصب کا بڑا نقصان ہو تو مالک کی ملکیت ختم ہو جائے گی، اور غاصب پر ضمان لازم ہو گا۔
Book of Usurpation: And upon the usurper is returning the usurped property. And if he claims its destruction, the judge detains him until he knows that if it were extant he would have produced it, then he passes judgment against him for its replacement. And usurpation applies to what is movable and transferable. And if he usurps real estate and it perishes in his hand, he is not liable according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said he is liable. And what is diminished by his action and his residence, he is liable for it in all of their statements. And when the usurped property perishes in the hand of the usurper by his action or without his action, he is liable for it. Then if it is diminished in his hand, upon him is liability for the diminution. And who slaughters the sheep of another, its owner has the choice: if he wishes, he makes him liable for its value and hands it over to him, (because it) invalidates most of its benefits, so its owner can make him liable for its full value. Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish "upon the usurper is returning the usurped property": "And whoever takes the stick of his brother, let him return it." Ibn Bashar did not say: Ibn Yazid. He said: The Messenger of Allah said. Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter of whoever takes something in jest, no. 5003. Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish "And if he usurps real estate and it perishes in his hand": From Sa'id ibn Zayd, from the Prophet, he said: "Whoever revives dead land, it is his, and there is no right for a wrongdoer's root." Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter of reviving dead land, no. 3073 / Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Chapter of what is mentioned about reviving dead land, no. 1378. Evidence (2): The hadith to establish "And if he usurps real estate and it perishes in his hand": From Salim, from his father, he said: The Prophet said: "Whoever takes from the earth anything without right, he will be swallowed up into seven earths on the Day of Resurrection." (Bukhari, Chapter of the sin of whoever wrongs something from the earth, no. 2454) Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish "And what is diminished by his action and his residence, he is liable for it in all of their statements": From Anas: "That the Prophet was with one of his wives, and one of the Mothers of the Believers sent with a servant a bowl containing food. She struck with her hand and broke the bowl. He held it together and put the food in it, and said: 'Eat.' And he detained the messenger and the bowl until they finished, then he gave the sound bowl and kept the broken one." (Bukhari, Chapter: If one breaks a bowl or something belonging to another, no. 2481) Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish "And who slaughters the sheep of another, its owner has the choice": From Abu Hurayrah, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: "There was a man among the Children of Israel called Jurayj, who was praying... So they came to him and broke his hermitage." Principle: If the usurped property is present with the usurper, then it is obligatory to return the very usurped property. And if he wishes, he makes him liable for its diminution. And someone who tears the garment of another with a small tear is liable for its diminution. And if he tears it with a large tear, then if the usurped property changes by the action of the usurper until its name and most of its benefits are lost, the ownership of the owner from it ceases and the usurper owns it and is liable for it to the end. And it is not permissible for him to benefit from it until he pays its replacement. And if he usurps silver or gold and mints it into dirhams or dinars or utensils, the ownership of its owner does not cease from it according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The usurpee has no claim on the minted dirhams and dinars, and upon him is the like of the silver that he usurped, and the usurper owns it. And whoever usurps a plank and builds upon it, the ownership of its owner ceases from it, and upon the usurper is its value. They (the people) brought him down and insulted him, so he performed ablution and prayed, then came to the boy and said: Who is your father, O boy? He said: The shepherd. They said: We will build your hermitage with gold. He said: No, only with clay. (Bukhari, Chapter: If one breaks a bowl or something belonging to another, 2482) Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish "And if the usurped property changes": Asim ibn Kulayb informed us, from his father, from a man of the Ansar, he said: We went out with the Messenger of Allah for a funeral. I saw the Messenger of Allah while he was at the grave instructing the digger: "Widen from the direction of his feet, widen from the direction of his head." When he returned, a woman's caller met him. He came and food was brought. He placed his hand, then the people placed, and they ate. Our fathers saw the Messenger of Allah chewing a morsel in his mouth, then he said: "I find the meat of a sheep that was taken without the permission of its owners." The woman sent: O Messenger of Allah, I sent to al-Baqi' to buy a sheep for me, but I did not find (one). So I sent to a neighbor of mine who had bought a sheep to send me with its price, but he was not found. So I sent to his wife, and she sent to me with it. The Messenger of Allah said: "Feed it to the captives." (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter of avoiding doubtful things, no. 3332; Sunan al-Daraqutni, Chapter of hunting, game, and foods, etc., no. 4763) Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish "And whoever usurps a plank and builds upon it": From Sa'id ibn Zayd, from the Prophet, he said: "Whoever revives dead land, it is his, and there is no right for a wrongdoer's root." (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter of reviving dead land) Principle: Imam Abu Hanifa: If a change occurs in the usurped property, the usurper becomes its owner, but its guarantee becomes obligatory upon him, and before payment of the guarantee, benefiting from it is not lawful, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i. Principle: If returning the usurped property causes great loss to the usurper, then the ownership of the owner ceases, and guarantee becomes obligatory upon the usurper.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn on usurpation (ghasb) begins by establishing the primary ruling: the usurper must return the very property seized. If he claims it was destroyed, the judge detains him pending investigation. The ruling applies only to movable property, as indicated by 'what is movable and transferable.' Immediately, an intra-Hanafi dispute arises regarding real estate: if usurped land perishes in the usurper's hands, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold no liability, while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds the usurper liable. However, for any damage caused by the usurper's own action or residence, all three agree on liability. The text then covers partial loss—if the property is diminished, the usurper compensates the decrease. Next, a special case: slaughtering another's sheep. Since the act destroys most benefits, the owner can choose to take the sheep (with compensation for the value) or claim full value. The commentary provides hadith proofs: the obligation to return is supported by the hadith 'return the stick,' and the ruling on real estate is supported by the hadith on reviving dead land and the severe warning against taking land unjustly. The passage continues with other cases—tearing a garment (small/large tear), change of identity (if the usurper transforms the item completely, ownership transfers to him but he must pay its value and cannot use it until payment), usurping silver and minting coins (Abu Hanifa says ownership unchanged, while the Sahibayn say the usurper owns the new coins and must pay an equivalent weight of silver), and building on a usurped plank (ownership transfers to the builder). The Urdu usul notes reiterate: if the property is present, return it; if change occurs, ownership transfers but with liability; and if returning would cause great loss, ownership may cease. Throughout, the Hanafi positions are grounded in hadith and rational reasoning.

Key Terms
تَغَيُّرُ الْعَيْنِ (taghayyur al-ayn): Change of the property's identity or nature.
زَوَالُ الْمِلْكِ (zawal al-milk): Cessation of ownership.
الْخِيَارُ (al-khiyar): Option or choice given to the owner in certain cases, such as after slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what happens if someone usurps a plank (sajah) and builds it into a structure?
A) The plank must be removed and returned.
B) Ownership of the plank transfers to the builder, and he must pay its value.
C) The owner can demand the plank back, and the builder must demolish the structure.
D) The builder is not liable for the plank.

Key Takeaway
When usurped property is completely transformed (loss of name and benefits), ownership transfers to the usurper, who must pay the value and cannot use it before payment.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Usurped Silver Beaten into Coins
Presents differing rulings on ownership change when usurped metal is transformed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on ownership of transformed usurped property and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When usurped silver is transformed, Abu Hanifa preserves the owner's right; the Sahibayn treat it as a transfer of ownership.

This passage records a classic intra-madhhab difference within the Hanafi school. The case involves a usurper who takes raw silver or gold and then converts it into coins or utensils. The central question is whether the original owner still owns the transformed object. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to trace how changes in property form affect legal ownership.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Imam Abu Hanifa holds. According to the text, the owner's ownership does not cease (lam yazul milku malikiha 'anha). He may claim the specific coins or vessels.
Note that Abu Hanifa focuses on the continuity of the original substance (ayn).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imāmān Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) disagree. They rule that the usurper owns the new objects and the original owner only gets a like amount (mithl) of the material.
The Sahibayn consider the transformation a fundamental change (taghayyur) that severs the original ownership.
3
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the owner can demand the specific coins; under the Sahibayn, the owner only receives an equivalent in weight and purity, and the usurper keeps the specific coins.
This difference affects whether the owner gets the exact property back or just compensation.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school for such cases is Abu Hanifa's view, especially when the original material remains identifiable. Later manuals generally prefer it.
This lesson's text does not explicitly state the tarjih, but the school's practice is known from later works like al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ غَصَبَ فِضَّةَ أَوْ ذَهَبًا فَضَرَبَهَا دَرَاهِمَ أَوْ دَنَانِيرَ أَوْ آنِيَةً لَمْ يَزُلْ مِلْكُ مَالِكِهَا عَنْهَا عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا سَبِيلَ لِلْمَغْصُوبِ مِنْهُ عَلَى الدَّرَاهِم وَالدَّنَانِيرِ الْمَضْرُوبَةِ وَعَلَيْهِ مِثْلُ الْفِضَّةِ الَّتِي غَصَبَهَا وَمَلَكَهَا الْغَاصِبُ
And if he usurped silver or gold and beat it into dirhams or dinars or vessels: the ownership of its owner does not cease from it according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: There is no recourse for the one from whom it was usurped over the dirhams and dinars that are beaten, and he owes the like of the silver which he usurped, and the usurper owns it.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) within the school regarding the transformation of usurped property. The text presents the ruling when someone usurps a raw material such as silver or gold and then transforms it into coins or utensils. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the original owner’s ownership does not cease; he may still claim the specific coins or vessels from the usurper. However, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), the original owner has no right to the transformed object; instead, the usurper becomes its owner and is liable to pay the like (mithl) of the silver or gold originally usurped. The practical effect (thamarah al-khilaf) is: under Abu Hanifa, the owner can demand the return of the actual coins; under the Sahibayn, the owner only receives an equivalent amount. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the school is generally that of Imam Abu Hanifa in matters of property where the identity (ayn) can still be traced, but this text does not specify tarjih; it merely records the divergent views.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Unlawful taking and control of someone else's property without permission.
مثل (mithl): An equivalent in quality and quantity; compensation in kind for fungible goods.
ملك (milk): Legal ownership and dominion over property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa in the passage, if someone usurps silver and beats it into dirhams, what is the ruling on ownership?
A) The usurper becomes the owner and must pay the value.
B) The owner's ownership ceases because the form changed.
C) The owner retains ownership and can claim the dirhams.
D) The owner has no recourse and must accept compensation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the transformation of usurped property does not automatically transfer ownership if the substance remains identifiable; Abu Hanifa’s view preserves the owner's right, which is the mufta bihi.

Owner's Option When Usurped Property Increases
Owner's option when usurped property recovered after compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the owner has the option (khiyar) when a usurped object is recovered with increased value after compensation.

Core Idea
The owner's option depends on how the compensation amount was determined: if based on the usurper's own admission, the owner chooses; otherwise the compensation is final.

In the book of Ghasb (Usurpation), Imam al-Quduri presents a precise ruling on a scenario where the usurper has already paid compensation and the property later appears with a higher value. The ruling hinges on the basis on which the compensation was determined, granting the owner a choice only in one specific case. This lesson will help you understand the legal reasoning behind the option (khiyar) and its limitations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The usurped property is recovered after the usurper has already paid compensation (daman), and its current value exceeds the amount paid.
2
Distinguish the basis of compensation
The text lists four ways the compensation amount could have been set: (1) based on the owner's own statement, (2) based on evidence (bayyinah), (3) based on the usurper's refusal to take an oath (nukul), or (4) based on the usurper's own statement accompanied by his oath.
3
Apply the khiyar rule
If the compensation was set by any of the first three methods, the owner has no khiyar—the guarantee is final. Only if the amount was determined by the usurper's own statement with his oath does the owner gain the option to either enforce the guarantee or take back the property and return the compensation.
The usurper's own admission under oath is considered less reliable, so the owner is given a second chance.
4
Determine the owner's options
If the khiyar exists, the owner may either 'amda al-daman' (enforce the guarantee and keep the compensation) or 'akhadha al-'ayn wa radd al-'iwad' (take the property and return the compensation). The choice is his.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ ظَهَرَتْ الْعَيْنُ وَقِيمَتُهَا أَكْثَرُ مِمَّا ضَمِنَ، وَقَدْ ضَمِنَهَا بِقَوْلِ الْمَالِكِ أَوْ بَيِّنَةٍ أَقَامَهَا أَوْ بِنُكُولِ الْغَاصِبِ عَنْ الْيَمِينِ فَلَا خِيَارَ لِلْمَالِكِ وَإِنْ كَانَ ضَمِنَهَا بِقَوْلِ الْغَاصِبِ مَعَ يَمِينِهِ فَالْمَالِكُ بِالخَيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَمْضَى الصَّمَانَ ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَ الْعَيْنَ وَرَدَّ الْعِوَضَ
If the object appears and its value is more than what was guaranteed, and he guaranteed it based on the owner's statement, or on proof he established, or on the usurper's refusal to take the oath, then the owner has no option. But if he guaranteed it based on the usurper's statement with his oath, then the owner has the option: if he wishes, he may enforce the guarantee; if he wishes, he may take the object and return the compensation.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Book of Ghasb (Usurpation) by Imam al-Quduri. It addresses the situation where the usurped property is recovered after the usurper has already paid compensation (daman). The ruling distinguishes how the compensation was determined. If based on the owner's valuation, evidence, or the usurper's refusal to swear, the compensation is final and the owner has no khiyar. But if the usurper himself stated the amount with his oath, the owner may choose between accepting the compensation or taking back the property and returning the compensation.

Key Terms
الخيار (al-khiyar): The legal option to choose between two alternatives
الضمان (al-daman): Compensation or guarantee for the usurped property

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which case does the owner have the option (khiyar) when the usurped property appears with increased value?
A) When the usurper paid compensation based on the owner's statement
B) When the usurper paid compensation based on his own statement with his oath
C) When the usurper paid compensation based on evidence
D) When the usurper refused to take the oath

Key Takeaway
The validity of the owner's option (khiyar) when a usurped object returns with increased value depends solely on whether the compensation was determined by the usurper's own admission under oath.

Offspring and Fruit of Usurped Property as Amanah
Ruling on offspring and fruit as amanah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the offspring of a usurped slave and the fruit of a usurped garden are amanah in the usurper's hand and identify the two conditions under which the usurper becomes liable.

Core Idea
Offspring and fruit of usurped property are trusts – no liability unless transgression or withholding after demand.

This lesson examines a precise ruling from Al-Quduri regarding the legal status of the natural increase (offspring and fruit) of usurped property. While the usurped property itself is mazmun (guaranteed), its generically similar increase is treated as amanah – a trust for which the usurper bears no loss unless he acts wrongfully. This principle balances ownership rights with the practical reality that the usurper holds possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property
What are the two examples of increase mentioned? (Offspring of female slave, fruit of garden)
2
State the default ruling
What is the legal status of these increases in the usurper's hand? (Amanah)
3
State the consequence of amanah
What is the default liability for loss? (No daman)
4
List the exceptions
What two actions change the ruling to liability? (Transgression (ta'addi) or demand by owner followed by withholding)
5
Apply the rule
Consider a scenario: the fruit rots naturally – no liability; the usurper sells the fruit – transgression, so liability.
Think about other examples: animal offspring, natural increase.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَوَلَدُ الْمَغْصُوبَةِ وَلَاؤُهَا وَثَرَةُ الْبُسْتَانِ الْمَغْصُوبِ أَمَانَةٌ فِي يَدِ الْغَاصِبِ إِنْ هَلَكَتْ فَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَعَدَّى فِيهَا أَوْ يَطْلُبَهَا مَالِكُهَا فَيَمْنَعَهُ إِيَّاهَا
And the offspring of the usurped (female slave) and her loyalty (for inheritance) and the fruit of the usurped garden are a trust (amanah) in the hand of the usurper. If they perish, there is no liability on him unless he transgresses regarding them, or the owner demands them and he withholds them from him.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This ruling explains that the offspring of a usurped female slave and the produce of a usurped garden are considered amanah (trust) in the hands of the usurper. They are not guaranteed by the usurper unless he commits a transgression (ta'addi) against them, or if the owner demands them and the usurper refuses to return them (i.e., becomes a usurper of those items as well). This is based on the principle that the usurper is liable for the principal property but not for its generically similar increase unless he acts wrongfully.

Key Terms
أمانة (amanah): A trust; property held without liability for loss unless caused by negligence or transgression
الغصب (al-ghasb): Usurpation; wrongful taking of another's property

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does the usurper become liable for the offspring of a usurped female slave?
A) If the offspring dies
B) If the owner demands the offspring and the usurper withholds it
C) If the offspring is male
D) The usurper is never liable

Key Takeaway
The offspring and fruit of usurped property are amanah; only transgression or demand-withhold creates liability.

Liability for Decrease in a Usurped Slave's Value Due to Childbirth
Ruling on compensation for decrease via childbirth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the usurper's liability when a female slave gives birth and identify the condition under which the child's value compensates the decrease.

Core Idea
The usurper owes for the decrease, but if the child's value covers it, the child replaces the compensation.

This passage from al-Quduri addresses a specific scenario in ghasb (usurpation): a female slave is taken wrongfully, and during that period she gives birth, which reduces her market value. The ruling clarifies how the usurper's liability is discharged if the value of the child (which belongs to the owner) equals or exceeds the loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the decrease in value of a female slave due to childbirth. The ruling is that this decrease is the liability (daman) of the usurper.
The decrease is attributed to the usurper because it occurred under his unlawful possession.
2
Apply the exception condition
If the value of the child (born to the owner) is sufficient to cover the full decrease, then the child is taken as compensation and the usurper's liability is discharged.
If the child's value is less than the decrease, the usurper remains liable for the shortfall.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ال وَمَا نَقَصَتْ الْجَارِيَةُ بِالْوِلَادَةِ فَمِنْ ضَمَانِ الْغَاصِبِ فَإِنْ كَانَ فِي قِيمَةِ الْوَلَدِ وَفَاء بِهِ جُبِرَ النُّقْصَانُ بِالْوَلَدِ وَسَقَطَ ضَمَانُهُ عَنْ الْغَاصِبِ
And whatever decrease occurs in the female slave due to childbirth is from the liability of the usurper. If the value of the child suffices to cover it, the decrease is compensated by the child, and the usurper's liability drops from the usurper.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This ruling deals with a female slave (jariyah) who is usurped and then gives birth, causing a decrease in her market value. The usurper is liable for that decrease. However, if the value of the child is sufficient to offset the decrease, then the child (which belongs to the owner) is taken as compensation for the decrease, and the usurper's liability is discharged. This is based on the principle that benefit and harm from the same cause can be offset.

Key Terms
الجارية (al-jariyah): A female slave
الولادة (al-wiladah): Childbirth
ضمان الغاصب (daman al-ghasib): Liability of the usurper to compensate for loss or damage to the usurped property

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the value of the child covers the decrease in the slave's value?
A) The usurper must also pay the child's value
B) The decrease is compensated by the child and the usurper's liability ends
C) The owner may keep both the slave and the child and demand compensation
D) The usurper is still liable for the full decrease

Key Takeaway
The usurper is liable for the decrease from childbirth, but if the child's value covers it, the child compensates and liability ends.
